## 9229

B"H, 7 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the "Torah U'Miktzo'a" Vocational High School, Bnei Brak, may they live:

Shalom u'Bracha!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter, in which you write of your impressions from the sicha you heard from your esteemed principal, shlita, on 19 Kislev, regarding the teachings of Chassidus Chabad and its concepts.

And based on the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, that "action is the essential thing," which is surely the line of conduct in your daily lives as well, I am confident that the aforementioned impression will be expressed in matters of practical action. That is to say, conduct in accordance with the teachings of Chassidus, which demands an added measure of beauty and care in the fulfillment of mitzvos—and in particular, the mitzvah of Talmud Torah, which is equivalent to them all—to increase in it with persistence, diligence, and vitality. For there is nothing that can stand before the will.

This is especially true when it concerns youth, from whom the demand is many times greater: firstly, because they are not distracted by the worries of earning a livelihood; and secondly, because these are the years in which one lays and fortifies the foundation for one’s entire life. This is similar to a building in the literal sense, where the entire strength of the structure—and even its beauty, perfection, and so on—depends upon a strong and solid foundation that can withstand all changes, upheavals, and so on.

Therefore, every effort and exertion is worthwhile to invest more and more energy and vitality during these precious years to strengthen the foundations of Torah and mitzvos, which are the true and eternal foundations for all the years to come— the days of our years, seventy years, or by reason of strength, eighty years, and may his days be one hundred and twenty years.

You are surely aware of the takanah of the monthly Tehillim cycle, to be recited each day after Shacharis, and I trust you are following this practice.

It is appropriate that those who have not had their tefillin checked within the last twelve months should do so now.

With blessings for success in the study of our holy Torah, the Torah of truth, in a manner that the study will be in accordance with the instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory: study that leads to the action of fulfilling mitzvos with hiddur, and for the fulfillment of your hearts' desires for good and for blessing.

## 930

B"H, 14 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with communal needs, etc.,
R' Yitzchak Isaac Wagner,

Shalom u’Bracha!

In response to your letter in which you ask my opinion regarding the [time] of the writing of the Mishnah:

You yourself mention in your letter the various opinions on this matter: the view of Rashi (Eruvin 62b) and many of our Sages, of blessed memory, that even in the days of the Amora Abaye, "there was not a single word of Halacha written down in their time, except for Megillas Taanis"; and the view of the Rambam (in his introduction to Sefer HaYad HaChazakah) that "Rabbeinu HaKadosh compiled the entire Sefer HaMishnah... and it was revealed throughout all of Yisrael, and they wrote it all down."

It is understood that one should not insert oneself between such great mountains. Although, on the face of it, there would be room to suggest that the Rambam, who saw the writings of the Geonim, held his opinion based on the Iggeres of Rabbeinu Sherira Gaon, and perhaps Rashi had not seen this Iggeres (as he was located far from Bavel, etc., unlike the Rambam), and therefore wrote as he did—whereas he might have written differently had the Iggeres come into his hands.

However, many of the later Sages, of blessed memory, hold the same view as Rashi on this, and have brought proofs for it. These matters are detailed in the sefarim that discuss the aforementioned question.

Since you do not mention anything regarding yourself and your family, may they live and be well, I hope this is a sign that all is well with you. And since your letter was written during Chanukah, may it be His will that this also be fulfilled in you—[increasing and continuing] from time to time—including also that you increase your activities in spreading Yiddishkeit. For our Sages, of blessed memory, have said that we [increase] in matters of holiness, especially regarding those who have influence in their surroundings; others will see them and do likewise, and this is well understood.

With respect and blessing.

P.S. Regarding your writing about meeting on the upcoming Motzaei Shabbos or the following Sunday morning: since I am not in my office at those times, I rely [on the ruling] of our Sages, of blessed memory, that the Holy One, blessed be He, joins a good thought to an action. May it be His will as if we had met face-to-face, and may your visit to Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, be successful, and may your journey there and back be in a good and auspicious hour.

## 9332

B"H, 15 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the participants of the Siyum HaTorah celebration on Sunday, Parshas Va'era, the coming week, and foremost among them, Rabbi Yitzchak Dovid Wein, may he live:

Peace and blessing!

I received with pleasure the news regarding the completion of the Sefer Torah, and that you are holding a celebration for the "completion of the Torah."

Surely, even though there will be a conclusion and completion of the Torah regarding the writing of the scroll, there is the well-known expression: "We juxtapose the beginning to the completion constantly," meaning that one begins immediately to study it with greater intensity and strength—a study —as instructed by the Sages of the Torah—that leads to action, the fulfillment of the mitzvos with beauty and care.

This strengthens the hope that each and every one of those completing the scroll will, from this day forward, increase their Torah study in the shul and beis medrash by establishing a regular shiur in Torah study, and specifically the study of the halachos required for daily life—a study that will influence the conduct of each and every person in their own home as well, for themselves and their families, may they live.

For it is through the study of Torah and the fulfillment of its mitzvos that we draw near and hasten the true and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, fulfilling the promise in this week’s parsha: "And I will take you to Me for a people... and I will bring you to the land... and I will give it to you as an inheritance, I am Hashem," such that "as in the days of your exodus from the land of Egypt, I will show you wonders" in the imminent Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and blessing.

## 933

[933](#_ftn_255)

B"H, 15 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the 28th annual dinner
of Merkaz Yeshivos Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
May Hashem keep them alive

Greetings and blessings!

This year’s celebration of the central Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch also marks the seventieth anniversary since the founding of the first Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim in Lubavitch.

It is written: **"This is the Torah — man,"** which indicates that a Jew and Torah are one entity. Similarly, a Torah institution is in many respects comparable to a Jew: both undergo the same exile, the same wanderings and experiences, until the intent of the Divine Providence is carried out.

Seventy years is a period in a human life — **"The days of our years are seventy years,"** such that afterward, a new period begins: the period of "strength" (*gevuros*), eighty years.

The Lubavitcher Yeshiva has passed through this period of 70 years, and it was one of the most difficult and turbulent periods in the Jewish exile. Yet, through the kindness of Hashem Yisbarach, the Lubavitcher Yeshiva stands today at the center of a chain of Lubavitcher yeshivos in many parts of the world, at a peak of development and creativity. It is clearly evident that they are fulfilling their mission and intent according to the foresight and assurance of the great and holy founders — [the mission](#_ftn_258) to educate students as **Temimim**, in the **complete** (*temimah*) Torah (**complete** Jews, in a **complete** Torah), to be **"lamps to illuminate"** with the light of **"the candle is a mitzvah and the Torah is light,"** both in the revealed aspects of Torah and in the inner dimensions of Torah, [illuminating](#_ftn_262) the path toward Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

Now, Yeshiva Tomchei Temimim is entering a new period, and as with all matters of Torah and holiness, this signifies an elevation to an even higher level: **"We elevate in matters of holiness."**

It is to be hoped that all friends of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch will know how to appreciate the historical moment of such a conclusion and beginning in the brilliant history of this unique Torah institution, which is one of the strongest pillars of Jewish life.

It is also to be hoped that all friends and supporters, and especially the *askanim* of the Yeshiva, will know how to appreciate the great *zechus* they have as partners in the achievements of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch, and will strengthen and expand this partnership — the historical [partnership](#_ftn_264) of Yissachar and Zevulun — to the greatest degree, in the new period of **"strength"** into which the Lubavitcher Yeshiva is now entering.

May the Ribono shel Olam grant you all, together and each individually, success in the aforementioned partnership, and through it, bless you with everything you need, materially and spiritually.

With honor and with blessings for outstanding success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9334

B"H, 15 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished Rabbi, a man of action and fine character, etc.,
Rabbi Avraham Sofer,

Shalom u’Bracha!

A few days ago, I received the Tanya translated into Italian, already bound. I am certain that you, too, have received it from Milan, and I am confident that it gave you great satisfaction to see that your efforts in this matter have borne good fruit—not only that it was brought to fruition, but that it was produced beautifully on the outside as well, although I am not familiar with the standard of external presentation for such books in Italy. It is my hope that the translation itself is also well-suited to the spirit of Italian Jewry.

This is one of the reasons for the delay in acknowledging your letter; I was hoping from day to day that I would receive the aforementioned Tanya so that I could inform you of it. Regarding what you wrote concerning payment to Prof. Colombo, I have conveyed this to Milan. Since I do not know what sums are involved, nothing has been written about it yet. If you have any comments or opinions on this, I would appreciate it if you would write to me. And if one might say so, this too is included in the statement of our Sages which begins, "One who is engaged in a mitzvah is told, 'Finish it.'"

It is surprising that I have heard nothing from you regarding what we discussed when you were here concerning participation in the printing costs of the Torah of the Rishonim, a project in which you are involved. As I recall, it was discussed that you would inform me about this in the month of Tishrei. Regarding all such matters (the publication of the Torah of the [Rishonim kemalachim](#_ftn_269)), the sooner the better, especially in the case of someone like yourself, where experience has shown that when you print a book in this field, you immediately begin preparations for the printing of another.

With respect and blessing for good news regarding all that has been said and all that was written in your letter, with joy, goodness of heart, and health.

## 935

[15 Teves, 5728]

However:

1) The army of enemies stands at their borders from all directions, may Hashem protect us, and only fear is holding them back, and to the wise it is understood.

2) The danger [from the north](#_ftn_271) will open, G-d forbid – it is much greater now than before. However, the point is not to frighten Bnei Yisrael, may they live and be well, but rather to awaken and encourage them, for everything depends on teshuvah and maasim tovim that are in the hands of each and every one – and specifically the [mitzvah](#_ftn_272) that instills awe and fear, etc.

– [The question from the outset is puzzling:

1) Seemingly, the question should come from those who labored **the most** in the Mivtza Tefillin during the war, and consequently their question is: "Is it possible now to rest a little in this?" Yet, it comes specifically from those who **at that time** did **nothing** in this regard, **nor in the rest of the 613 mitzvos.**

2) **And it is explained** that the blessing of Hashem (and the verdict of the Heavenly Beis Din) comes based on the maasim tovim that they will do in the future, not only because of the maasim tovim of the past. And Bnei Yisrael, who are believers, also believe that the conduct of the nations of the world below depends on the conduct of their ministering angel above, **and that is the main thing**, and it is in this that the Heavenly verdict is relevant and effective.]

And in this current matter, the success in this has only further inflamed the heirs of the sect of Avigdor and his sect to spread, etc. – in contrast to the spreading of the wellsprings of the teachings of Chassidus. And to the wise it is understood.

## 9336

[9336](#_ftn_274)

[Teves, 5728]

(1) The intention of speaking about this is, Heaven forbid, not to frighten—on the contrary, it is forbidden to cause distress, and it is not a matter of frightening Bnei Yisrael shlita—but rather the intention is solely to awaken and encourage them, knowing that everything depends on teshuvah and maasim tovim, etc. Therefore, we speak of this in public and convey these two points in detail. (2) And to find the appropriate time for this in the broadcast during the week and in the broadcast on Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh.

It is worth conveying in general that someone asked such a question, and the response to this is that it adds emphasis to the entire matter of the demand of the hour to strengthen the Mivtza Tefillin campaign.

(3) And to add, **briefly**, that one who contemplates the recent events sees once again how the verse is fulfilled: "The kindness of the nations is a sin." And that there is no room at all to err [by saying] "my strength and the might of my hand has made me this wealth," etc. And to the wise, a word is sufficient. Rather, Bnei Yisrael must create the channels and vessels for Hashem’s blessings—Torah and mitzvos—and Hashem, who performed open miracles in the past, will do so now as well, in a revealed and manifest good. ## 940

24 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter...

And on the day of the *histalkus* and *hillula* of the Alter Rebbe—at the time of the *histalkus*, there is a ["revelation](#_ftn_289) of the illumination of the very essence of his root, in the highest of heights, at the most exalted level, far above"—and there is revealed and illuminated from above to below ["all](#_ftn_290) [the labor](#_ftn_291) [of man](#_ftn_292) that his soul labored during his lifetime"—a supreme *tzaddik* who served Hashem with love and *mesiras nefesh* to Hashem—and through this, "the *chesed* of Hashem shines from eternity to eternity upon those who fear Him, and He works salvations within the earth."

Now, every person is born [to labor](#_ftn_293) (his own), and our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe is indeed as his name implies, and so is his labor. As the [Baal Shem Tov](#_ftn_294) said: His name is Shneur—[*shnei*](#_ftn_295) *ohr*—two lights—he will illuminate [the Torah](#_ftn_296) of the revealed and the Torah of the hidden.

And according to the [principle](#_ftn_297) (and the law) that the mention and inclusion of two things in one word indicates their union, and even a union in perfection—it is understood here as well that the intent is [the connection](#_ftn_298) and union of the two lights and their unification, for it is one Torah.

Thus, year after year, these [days](#_ftn_299) (as they are) are remembered (properly, and then all the illuminations and *hemshechim* are brought about).

And the body follows the head: all those who study his Torah—the revealed Torah and the inner dimension of Torah (*Toras HaChassidus*)—in the manner mentioned above, and who strive to walk "in the straight path which he taught us, and we shall walk in his ways [etc.](#_ftn_300)."

* * *

Now, since [Kudsha Brich Hu](#_ftn_301), the Torah, and Yisrael are bound together, and each is both hidden and revealed, it is understood that the connection and union of the hidden and revealed aspects of Torah, and the connection and union of the hidden and revealed aspects of [Yisrael](#_ftn_302), are dependent [upon one another](#_ftn_303). Through both of them comes the connection, as it were, and the union of the hidden and revealed aspects of [Kudsha Brich Hu](#_ftn_304).

Through all of this, they connect and unite the entire creation with its [soul](#_ftn_305)—the light and word of Hashem that brings it into being, enlivens it, and sustains it.

This is the *avodah* upon which ["depends](#_ftn_306) the entire mystery of faith":

[Know](#_ftn_307) this day and take it to your heart that Hashem is the G-d in the heavens above and on the earth below; there is nothing else.

With blessings,

M. Schneerson

Due to circumstances, the letter was delayed [until](#_ftn_308) the Tenth of Shevat—and the day itself causes things to happen in the manner of all the above, for it is the day of the *histalkus* and *hillula* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe—Erev Shabbos Kodesh, after midday.

* * *

[On the day](#_ftn_309) of the *hillula*, the Tenth of Shevat, the [Tanya](#_ftn_310) printed in Australia was received. Many thanks.

I spoke with the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing man, involved in communal affairs, energetic and accomplished, etc., R' Shneur Chaim HaKohen Gutnick, that it would be worthwhile for you to publish another edition of the Tanya—in [pocket](#_ftn_311) format. Since you will not be pressed for time now, you can surely strive to ensure the new edition is most magnificent in every detail (paper, printing, binding, and the like).

Although it is worthwhile to begin preparations for printing the new edition immediately, it is not worthwhile to publicize it until the first edition is sold.

As my participation in this publication, I have given Rabbi Gutnick a sum of one hundred and one dollars ($101).

* * *

[As is my custom](#_ftn_312)—regarding additions to the encyclopedia—see *Hiddur Mitzvah*. Since the Alter Rebbe brings [the verse](#_ftn_313) ("This is my G-d and I will glorify Him"), it implies that he holds it is a Torah-level obligation. He also cites [the laws of] **Tzitzis**. And see *Me'asef LeChol HaMachanos* there. **And see references there.**

* * *

[I acknowledge](#_ftn_314) receipt of your letter from Motzaei Shabbos Vayechi (and the enclosure, and many thanks for the *nachas* it caused) and the *pidyon nefesh* therein will be read at an auspicious time at the holy gravesite.

And on the day of the *histalkus*...

With *mazal tov* wishes for the marriage of your grandson, R' M.A., may he build a faithful home in Israel.

* * *

[I acknowledge](#_ftn_315) receipt of your letter and the proofreading of the *Likkutei Biurim* on Tanya. May your strength be fortified, and the merit of the many depends on you.

And on the day of the *histalkus*...

With blessings for success in the publication of the aforementioned book, which will certainly also assist in *hafatzas hamaayanos*—and for good tidings in all of this.

* * *

[With blessings](#_ftn_316) for success in Torah study—revealed and Chassidus—and to be a [living example](#_ftn_317).

* * *

[I acknowledge](#_ftn_318) receipt of your letter from the day of "Teves" and the enclosure. Certainly, in the future as well, you should write in detail—simply the reality as it is—and many thanks in advance.

And on the day of the *histalkus*...

Did you receive the institutions' [funds] from the *aliyah* of Morocco?

With blessings for great success in the network of your institutions and in general.

## 9401

[9401](#_ftn_319)

B"H, 28 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Dr. Sachs, Director of the Ophthalmology Department
Assaf Harofeh Hospital, Tzrifin, Doar Be'er Yaakov

Greetings and blessings!

Your letter of January 7th was received in due time. Although I do not have funds at my disposal for these purposes, as an exceptional measure—since you also reached out to me in an exceptional manner—I have instructed my secretariat to fulfill your request as much as possible, and I hope that you have already received the materials you requested.

On this occasion, it is a pleasant duty for me to express my gratitude for the medical care you provided to Mr. D.S., and, more importantly, for the attention and gracious demeanor shown by you and your assistants. It is surely unnecessary to emphasize the great [importance](#_ftn_320) a patient places on the pleasant countenance of a physician. And even though [the reward](#_ftn_321) of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself—the satisfaction of the doctor who has fulfilled his duty to heal the sick, etc.—it is nonetheless my duty and a mitzvah incumbent upon me to express my satisfaction with the news I have received regarding this.

May it be the will of Hashem that, since we live in a time when there are, for the time being, many who are in need of healing in general, and especially in the field in which you specialize—ophthalmology—you will succeed in healing the sick, leading to their complete recovery. And may it also be His will that you utilize your influence to open blind eyes regarding the light of Torah and its illumination, to see that this light is good, so that each and every one of them, and of us, may realize it in their lives, even in the gray days—in the style of the prophet: "Lift up your eyes on high and see who created these" (Yeshayahu 40:26), and as the verses continue there: "Why do you say, O Yaakov, and speak, O Yisrael, 'My way is hidden from Hashem,' etc.? But those who hope in Hashem shall renew their strength; they shall mount up with wings as eagles, etc." And indeed, **the inhabitants of our Holy Land, [the land](#_ftn_322) upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year to the end of the year, have seen this even with physical eyes in the months that have passed.**

With respect and blessing, and regards to your assistants.

## 9442

[9442](#_ftn_323)

B"H, 28 Teves, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Schneur Zalman, may he live, Maschari,

Peace and Blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 20th of Teves and those preceding it. I thank you once again for your good practice of informing me of the activities in the Chabad movement, your participation in them, and your efforts to recruit more supporters and participants. For beyond the general requirement to strive [to ascend](#_ftn_324) in holiness in all matters of goodness, the situation in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, demands elevation after elevation. And since [Hashem](#_ftn_325) does not deal tyrannically with His creatures, He provides the ability to fulfill this demand.

Regarding what you wrote at the end of your letter, that you have a feeling there is a lack of coordination between the various factors working for Chabad: since you wrote this on the spot and feel this way, and you view matters with a favorable eye, there is likely a basis for what you write. However, on the other hand, I must add immediately that since we are dealing with living individuals—and especially in our era, which specifically demands an increase in vitality, enthusiasm, and so on—it is entirely not worthwhile to intervene too much. When one makes an honest assessment, perhaps it is better to overlook a lack of coordination—which there is hope will improve on its own through self-awakening—provided that there is a sense of independence among the workers, in the spirit of "the jealousy of scholars increases wisdom" [kinas sofrim tarbeh chochmah](#_ftn_326).

You do not write about your health, which implies that all is well.

With respect and blessing,

## 9443

[9443](#_ftn_327)

[Teves, 5728]

To the esteemed Rabbi, the G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished scholar, who disseminates Torah among the masses, a man of energy, etc., [Rabbi](#_ftn_328) Pinchas Mordechai, may he live and be well.

Peace and blessing!

Following our conversation regarding the weekly *daf* shiur via radio and the *Melaveh Malkah* to be held soon to strengthen this initiative:

I hereby reiterate my blessing that you succeed in establishing this shiur, strengthening it, and expanding it—both in quantity and in quality.

If, regarding several manifest things in creation, our Sages of blessed memory said that they were created for the sake of the Holy Temple of the Holy One, blessed be He, and it is only by virtue of this that the world also makes use of them (*Shemos Rabbah* 35:1), then how much more so is this true regarding a [hidden](#_ftn_329) and wondrous power in nature, which finds its rectification only by becoming a medium, a vessel, and a sanctuary for Him, may He be blessed. [And from the day](#_ftn_330) the Holy Temple was destroyed, the Holy One, blessed be He, has nothing in His world but the four cubits of *halacha* alone.

And in accordance with the [ruling of our Sages](#_ftn_331) that "study is great because it leads to action" (see the Rambam’s introduction to his *Peirush HaMishnayos* regarding the explanation of the statement "the Holy One, blessed be He, has nothing, etc."), [and "the beginning](#_ftn_333) of wisdom is the fear of Hashem," I hope that they will use this radio broadcast to emphasize and strengthen matters of *yiras shamayim* and the performance of *mitzvos* in actual practice. [And the end](#_ftn_334) of the matter—when all is heard: "Fear G-d and keep His *mitzvos*."

With appreciation and a blessing for success,

Menachem Schneerson

## 944

[944] 

[Teves, 5728]

I have received the telegram and your letters (dated 22 Teves, etc.). Regarding your wife, may she be well, follow the advice of a friendly doctor who has no personal interest in the matter.

I read with **great** astonishment in your letter the reason given by so-and-so for the difficulty with putting on tefillin—that it is forbidden for a person to harm animals. What relevance does this have to the matter at hand?! After all, tefillin are made (also) from the hides of animals that died of natural causes (see Shabbos 108a). **On the contrary**, according to the logic of the aforementioned individual—instead of leaving the animal hide to rot and be **lost**, or making it into shoes or **utensils** for the **feet** of a person or the like—

**It is incumbent upon him**—the mitzvah—to make of the hide something that will elevate the person and sanctify him, and even bind it as a "**splendor for his head**" [as the verse states]. And this is especially so according to what is explained in Kabbalah and Chassidus regarding what is accomplished through the mitzvah of tefillin **in all the worlds** (see Kuntres Acharon to the maamar "Dovid Zemirot," [130], and in many other places).

## 945

[945](#_ftn_338)

B"H, 5 Shevat, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, learned, and distinguished individual, a man of many accomplishments and fine character, [Rabbi](#_ftn_339) Shear Yashuv Cohen, may he live.

Greetings and blessings,

Your letter from Rosh Chodesh Teves, which arrived by regular mail, has just reached me. Many thanks for the clarification regarding the Old City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt and established, which you provided and informed me of.

Now, what has caused me concern—and, to my regret, more than mere concern—is not regarding the circles you consulted and whose response you conveyed, but rather those circles who, at the time of the conquest of the Old City, intervened, applied pressure, and insisted on their demands [regarding](#_ftn_340) the manner of the conquest. This was despite the fact that it was clear from the outset that this unusual approach would cost lives, etc. Their rationale was that they were supposedly forced into this because of the reaction of the nations—as if it is not known that the nations act in accordance with the [halachic](#_ftn_341) principle, "It is a known tradition that Eisav hates Yaakov," only that they change the pretext (*amla*)—as in the well-known interpretation of "truth" (*emes*)—to suit the situation. And suffice it to say. It is difficult to elaborate on a matter that causes deep sorrow over the blood that was spilled, and over the fact that, apparently, they continue to follow the line that the opinion of the nations is what determines our actions, G-d forbid.

Based on the above, it is understood how the reaction of the aforementioned circles will be if there is pressure from the nations. There is room for concern that they will see shadows of mountains as mountains. This is as was argued in certain circles in the capital city here, that it is astonishing to them that many of the Children of Israel are knocking on the doors of so-and-so, asking them not to apply so much pressure on this or that point—even on points where it had not occurred to them to apply pressure. And suffice it to say.

It is obvious that the above is not intended to act as a prosecutor against any of the Children of Israel; that is not my way or my conduct, etc., especially in light of the [teaching of the Mishnah](#_ftn_342), "Do not judge your **fellow until you have reached his place," etc. Rather, it is to clarify my opinion and stance regarding the situation and the attitude toward the Old City, as we discussed here.**

The aforementioned information regarding those circles was received by me in confidence, and therefore I did not mention them in our conversation here, as there was no necessity to do so. Furthermore, I thought that perhaps you were already aware of the aforementioned matter. However, since it appears from your letter that some points in this matter have escaped you, and the matter concerns practical action—in addition to the [commandment](#_ftn_343), "And you shall be clear before Hashem and before Israel"—I felt compelled to put them in writing, as I am confident that this will remain between us as a confidential letter.

I was especially pleased to hear about the gathering in the Chabad shul in the heart of the Old City of Jerusalem—the [city](#_ftn_344) that is joined together—which you wrote about at the end of your letter.

May it be the will of Hashem that, finally, even during the time of exile, [from Zion](#_ftn_345) shall go forth Torah and the word of Hashem from Jerusalem, both the Old and the New together. Through this, [as promised](#_ftn_346) by our Sages of blessed memory, Hashem will hasten the end of our exile, and we will merit the coming of our righteous Moshiach and the true and complete Redemption.

With respect and blessing,

## 9448

B"H, 6 Shevat, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished, a young man of high standing who seeks the good of his people, possessing noble character, a scion of an illustrious lineage, R' Schneur [Zalman](#_ftn_349) shlita,

Peace and blessing!

As the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, approaches this coming Erev Shabbos, I am, as is my custom, sending you some written words. In particular, I wish to recall the [merit](#_ftn_350) we had to be together at the farbrengen of 19 Kislev in the presence of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, and to sing together the nigun of our Alter Rebbe—this letter being written between the time of his yahrtzeit on 24 Teves and the yahrtzeit of 10 Shevat.

Based on what my father-in-law, the Rebbe, wrote [in his first letter](#_ftn_351) regarding the yahrtzeit of his father, that the shepherds of Israel do not abandon their flock, and [just as](#_ftn_352) he stood and served then, he stands and serves now on high, serving his flock within all of Israel—this follows [the well-known expression](#_ftn_353) of *ratzo v'shov*. The matter of *yichud* (unification) in his memory is the *ratzo*—ascending and uniting with the memory of the one whose yahrtzeit is being observed and his teachings—and the *shov*—drawing this down into actual deed in this physical and material world, to walk in the straight path that he taught us in his ways, and to walk in his paths, *netzach selah va'ed* (Iggeres HaKodesh of our Alter Rebbe regarding the passing of the Admur R' Menachem Mendel of Horodok, Iggeres HaKodesh in Tanya, Epistle 27).

Moving from one subject to a related one, I am enclosing herewith the recently published [Tanya](#_ftn_354) in its Italian translation, the language of Rome, of which it is said, "One nation shall be stronger than the other"—when this one (Rome) falls, Jerusalem, our holy city, shall be built.

This is one of the activities of *hafatzas hamaayanos chutzah*.

With appreciation, honor, and blessings for all good things.

## 9449

Mr. Yitzchak Ben-Lulu

For the entire [concept](#_ftn_358) of an army is founded upon discipline and the acceptance of the yoke to fulfill every order and command without questioning them, since this is not only for one's own benefit, but also for the benefit of all one's fellow soldiers and the entire army. And just like these things, and even more so, is the fulfillment of the commands of the Supreme Commander of the entire world, our Father in Heaven, the King of kings, the Holy One, blessed be He, who gave us—and each and every one of us—a Torah of life and mitzvos, [regarding which it is said](#_ftn_359), "that he shall live by them."

## 9450

9450

B"H, 9 Shevat, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed and distinguished individual, occupied in the needs of the community,
R' Moshe Avraham Yaffe
Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter dated 23 Teves reached me with a delay.

Regarding the distressing matter, the gathering, you surely received my telegram in due time. What I proposed—the content of which is seemingly clear—I will emphasize once again, with the preface as stressed in the telegram, that you did not ask for my opinion on the matter itself. Nevertheless, I felt obligated to point out to you, at the very least, the following point: that the gathering should not have been comprised of religious organizations, as this would arouse immense opposition, etc. In that same situation, when it was apparently no longer in your power to cancel it, I found the advice—albeit with great difficulty—that it should be a gathering of organizations connected to religion, such as synagogues, etc., and also organizations of **baalei-batim** (such as Young Israel), students (such as Yavneh), etc. It is understood and simple that there is no rectification in this at all when representatives of the **synagogues** of Young Israel were also invited, and even if their baalei-batim were also invited, **for the point concerns the gathering itself, and not who will deliver lectures there, or offer blessings, and the like; this is simple.**

My distress, which I mentioned in my telegram regarding your participation in the matter—and perhaps even more so than the participation, apparently from your signature on your aforementioned letter—has grown even further. For, in accordance with the promise of our Sages that "one mitzvah leads to another," there has been added to the character of the gathering a distinct partisan character, with all the trappings of a party and its methods, whatever it may be. First and foremost, as its name implies—a *miflagah* (party), from the language of *pilug* (division), *machlokes* (strife), and the separation of hearts—it is the absolute opposite of the goal, seemingly, of the gathering. And what is even more concerning—it is the complete opposite of what we need now, especially in these most recent months.

The booklet *Shana B'Shana* has just been received; many thanks for your thoughtfulness.

As I write this letter on the eve of the Yahrtzeit-Hilula of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, may it be the will of Hashem that each of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, be ignited by the ideals of the master of the Hilula, for which he sacrificed his life, and that we utilize for this purpose all the talents with which we have been gifted.

With respect and blessing.

M. Schneerson

## 9452

[9452](#_ftn_366)

By the Grace of Hashem, Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the activists and friends of the Beis Rivkah schools — in general, and to the participants in the annual Melaveh Malkah — in particular,

May Hashem be with them, may they live.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the notification regarding the upcoming annual Melaveh Malkah, Motzaei Shabbos Kodesh Parshas Yisro,

May the Ribono shel Olam grant that this undertaking — which is the only public event of its kind throughout the year — should be met with great success, both materially and spiritually.

Surely, each and every participant will bring with them to the Melaveh Malkah a significant measure of hisorerus from the [parsha](#_ftn_367) of that Shabbos, whose inner point is **Matan Torah** and **Kabbalas HaTorah**.

The connection and special merit of Jewish women and girls regarding Kabbalas HaTorah was indicated in the Torah itself, by the fact that the Ribono shel Olam commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to speak [first](#_ftn_368) with the women regarding Kabbalas HaTorah, and only afterwards with the men. Through this, the Torah emphasizes that the Jewish woman — the **akeres habayis** ("Beis Yaakov") — occupies a most vital place in securing and strengthening the daily Torah-life of the Jewish people!

It is understood that in order to fulfill this task to the fullest extent, the proper Torah-chinuch of Jewish girls must be secured first. From this, the life-essential necessity of the "Beis Rivkah" schools for girls is clear.

It so happens that just a few days ago was the yahrtzeit of my father-in-law, the Rebbe (10 Shevat), the founder of the Beis Rivkah institutions, who dedicated so much time and energy to their establishment and development. Each and every one of us who has united with the memory of the Baal HaHillula has surely renewed and redoubled our good resolutions to follow in his footsteps and continue his holy work in general, and for Beis Rivkah in particular, in an increased measure.

Today, **Rosh Hashanah La’ilanos**, reminds us once again that **ha’adam eitz hasadeh** — a person is like a tree. [Just](#_ftn_372) as it is life-essential for a tree and its future fruits that it receive the necessary nourishment and care while it is still very young, so too, and even more so, is it for a Jewish child.

I hope that all participants and friends of Beis Rivkah will make a special effort to provide the fullest assistance for the maintenance and expansion of Beis Rivkah, so as to be able to accept as many students as possible and educate each one of them to be a mashpi’ah, a madrichah, a mechaneches, and an akeres habayis — upon the purity of holiness.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9353

9353

B”H, Tuesday, the day on which “it was good” was doubled 
Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of the Gemilas Chasadim Society Shomrei Shabbos,
May Hashem protect them and may they live,

Peace and blessing!

In response to the announcement that the annual meeting and Melaveh Malkah will take place on Motzaei Shabbos Parshas Im Kesef Talveh Es Ami, as is your good custom year after year—

May it be the will [of Hashem] that it be at a good and successful time, and with an increase over last year—in accordance with the command (which is also a bestowal of strength): “We increase in matters of holiness.”

This year marks the completion of one hundred years since the maamar of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe Maharash, of blessed memory, of righteous memory, of blessed memory: “Vayikchu Li Terumah” (the beginning of the parsha which begins this Motzaei Shabbos)—“‘Me’ (Myself) you are taking”: Through the mitzvah of the contribution of gold and silver, etc., “Me”—meaning that which is in the state of “I, Hashem, have not changed”—you are taking.

He explains this based on the Midrash of our Sages on the verse “And these are the ordinances”: “This is what is written, ‘He tells His words, etc., His statutes and His ordinances to Yisrael’—the Holy One, blessed be He, does what He tells Yisrael to do. The Holy One, blessed be He, puts on tefillin, etc., and similarly with all the mitzvos.” The intent of the Midrash is that through the performance of the mitzvah of tefillin, one draws down the reality that the Holy One, blessed be He, puts on tefillin, and similarly with all the mitzvos. See there.

Based on the above, when Yisrael contribute from their silver and gold, etc., to fulfill the mitzvos of Hashem—matters of Torah and mitzvos in general, and Gemilas Chasadim, which is equivalent to all the mitzvos in particular—they are guaranteed that the Holy One, blessed be He, contributes and gives to them and to their households that which they require, in both material and spiritual terms, from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that you act in the aforementioned manner, and in a way that is ever-increasing, with joy and a glad heart.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9557

B"H, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5728

## 9458

9458

B"H, 1st day of Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

In such matters, [the law regarding a prutah is the same as the law regarding a maneh](#_ftn_399), as we discussed at length. This is different from a case where the person involved makes the claim himself, and the rest is understood.

Since every matter is governed by Hashgacha Pratis, I am taking this opportunity to send you what has recently been published regarding current affairs, which I hope will be of interest to you.

With respect and blessing.

## 959

[959](#_ftn_400)

By the Grace of Hashem, Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the 26th Annual Gathering of the "Natzivei HaYeshiva" of Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch in Montreal,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and Blessing!

We find ourselves in the days when we read in the Torah the parshios that speak of building the Mishkan.

Since the [Torah](#_ftn_401) is eternal, its directives (**Torah** comes from the word *horah*, meaning instruction) are eternally valid. This means that Jews can and must build a "Mishkan" and "Mikdash" for the Divine Shechinah at all times and wherever Jews may be.

The eternal validity of the Torah is strikingly emphasized by the [teaching](#_ftn_403) of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch, that the weekly parsha has a connection to the events of that specific week. The connection to the annual undertaking of the Yeshiva becomes clear when we consider that this undertaking is, in truth, also a matter of "building a Mishkan."

The inner point of building the Mishkan is that Jews took a portion of their gold, silver, and other material possessions, and with them built a holy place for the Divine Shechinah. In this way, they brought the Shechinah down to rest among them, **and together with the Shechinah, Divine blessings were brought down into all their affairs, both material and spiritual.**

In the present time, the Yeshiva occupies the place of the "Mishkan" and "Mikdash." The Yeshiva, where one learns the Ribono shel Olam’s Torah and davens daily with kavanah and mesiras nefesh—for [Torah](#_ftn_404) and tefillah are in place of the korbanos—is the "Mishkan" for the Divine Shechinah. This brings Divine blessings to all those who have a share in building and supporting this holy institution.

It is therefore to be hoped that all participants in the annual undertaking for the Lubavitcher Yeshiva in Montreal will emulate and display the spirit of self-sacrifice, with hislahavus and simcha, that the builders of the first Mishkan displayed. Surely, each one of you will know how to appreciate the great zechus of helping to build a Mishkan for the Divine Shechinah—an institution from which the light of Torah and mitzvos spreads out, illuminating and enlivening Jewish life in the near and far surroundings.

May this zechus stand by everyone and their families, may they live, to enjoy Divine blessings in everything they need, both materially and spiritually.

With blessings for success and good tidings, and a happy Purim in all respects.

## 970

[970](#_ftn_405)

[2 Rosh Chodesh Adar, 5728]

It is understood that in accordance with the change in the status of the Chassidim from the time this *Iggeret HaKodesh* was written the first time until the third time, there was room (and a need) for changes in its initial sections as well, including the addition, "in most towns and *minyanim* of *anash*."

On the face of it, the lengthiness of the *Iggeret HaKodesh* regarding the instruction to "complete the entire *Shas*, etc." implies that this was a novel directive. If so, it is possible that the opening of the *Iggeret HaKodesh*—"Opening with a blessing"—is a response to the "good news" that the request had been fulfilled. See *Likutei Dibburim* (Vol. 1, p. 89), which states that the *Iggeret HaKodesh* that opens with a blessing "was written and publicized ten years before the writing of *Iggeret HaKoton*"—that is, in the year 5749.

## 9762

[9762](#_ftn_410)

B"H, 7 Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the Chanukas HaBayis
of the Lubavitch Center in London,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha!

The dedication of the new building of the Lubavitch Center and the continuation of the celebratory ceremonies taking place during the week of the upcoming Purim days will surely be imbued with the nobility of spirit and the *hisorerus* of these auspicious days.

The focal point of the story of Purim is that the entire Jewish people—[as the verse states](#_ftn_411), "from young to old, children and women"—were in danger of a decree, until Mordechai HaYehudi came and gathered twenty-two thousand Jewish children, inflaming their hearts with words and education until they were prepared to engage in *mesiras nefesh* for their Yiddishkeit. It was then that the decree was nullified, [as recounted](#_ftn_412) by our Sages, of blessed memory.

It is a well-known [teaching](#_ftn_413) of our master, the Baal Shem Tov—founder of the general path of Chassidus, whose student’s student was our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch and father of the Chabad-Lubavitch system—who explained by way of *remez* the statement of the Mishnah (Megillah 17a): **"He who reads the Megillah *l'mafreah* (backwards/out of order)"**—meaning, one who thinks that the miracle happened then but not now—**"has not fulfilled his obligation."**

The lesson here is that all the themes of the Purim story are as potent now as they were then. And even though there is currently no danger of such a decree, *chas v’shalom*—and on the contrary, Hashem has granted success and Jews are able to live in tranquility and even in prosperity—this does not change the secret of the survival of the Jewish people: the proper education of Jewish sons and daughters to the point of *mesiras nefesh* for Yiddishkeit.

And this is the fundamental task of the Lubavitch Center in London: to gather Jewish children—children in the literal sense, and "children" in their knowledge of Hashem, His Torah, and His *mitzvos*—in order to reveal within them the inner dimension of their souls, their essence, and their core, so that they will recognize tangibly that they are—[as the verse](#_ftn_414) puts it—"children to Hashem your G-d." They will then continue the golden chain of their ancestors' tradition, to the point of *mesiras nefesh* for a life of Torah and *mitzvos*.

This *mesiras nefesh* naturally includes *mesiras nefesh* for another, coming to their aid in both their spiritual and material needs.

These traits were clearly highlighted in the character of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the Nasi of Chabad-Lubavitch of our generation, as is well known from the history of his life (for example: when he was only eleven years old, he was [imprisoned](#_ftn_415) and thrown into jail because he came to the aid of a Jew from the marketplace who was being mistreated by a gentile).

May it be the will of Hashem that the new building of the Lubavitch Center in London be filled with ["our young and our old, our sons and our daughters"](#_ftn_416) who walk in this spirit. Words cannot express the magnitude of the merit of all those who lent a hand to establish this new building, and who were and will be its supporters and participants in its activities; for every good deed of those educated and influenced in this house, and outside of it, is also to the credit and the portion and inheritance of each and every one of those who facilitate and perform these acts, may they live.

With respect and blessing for great success and for good tidings in all the aforementioned, and a happy Purim,

Menachem Schneerson

## 9463

9463

B"H, 7 Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Tzvi Itzkovitz, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, I receive regards from you via Rabbi Efraim Wolf, as well as from several of our anash in Lod and Kfar Chabad, regarding your interest in and assistance with all Chabad matters—to the point that you have even influenced your friends in this direction.

For this reason, I was particularly distressed to hear that your health was not in order, though it is my hope that by the time you receive this letter, you have already improved and returned to your work in the city and mother in Israel, the city of Lod, for the benefit of the city and its inhabitants—a benefit that is both material and spiritual. For while in every person the material and the spiritual are intertwined, for a Jew, this is with the emphasis on the dominance of the spiritual over the material, and of form over matter.

I would certainly be pleased if you would inform me of the improvement in your health in detail.

I ask your forgiveness for the delay in acknowledging receipt of your letter—or more accurately, the copy of your letter provided by Rabbi Wolf—which was delayed due to circumstances beyond my control. The main reason was that I did not have anything concrete in hand regarding the industrial matter we discussed during our conversation when you were here, as I also conveyed through Rabbi Wolf. Surely, by the time you receive this letter, you have already been visited by the diligent activist Mr. Avraham Parshan, **and have spoken with him regarding the industrial matter. May it be His will that, finally, the matter will come to fruition for the benefit of the many, in addition to the benefit of the few individuals who will be involved in it.**

 Our Sages have informed us that "merit is brought about through a meritorious person." These days before Purim are days when we are reminded once again, and with emphasis, of the well-known text: "All who hope in You (Hashem) shall not be shamed or disgraced forever, all who take refuge in You," with the preface that "You have been their salvation forever, and their hope in every generation." We are in need of all this even now. May it be His will that, just as in those days, at this time, we may also now see the frustration of the thoughts of all those who plot evil against the Jews, and the nullification of their counsel, and from redemption to redemption—the redemption of the collective and the individual through Mashiach Tzidkeinu.

With respect and a blessing for a happy Purim, with proper health and a good heart, and with regards to all your friends, may they live and be well.

## 9768

11 Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings,

After a long interval, I received your letter, and the pidyon will be read at the tziyun of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. May Hashem grant that you bring good news regarding this and your personal situation.

It is self-understood that I am pained that you did not mention anything regarding a shidduch. Apparently, the reason for the silence is that there is no change in the matter. Yet, there is the promise "you have labored and found," but there must be true labor in searching for a suitable shidduch.

Since I have already written many times on this subject, I do not wish to repeat myself, only to recall the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory: "Chatan" (groom) — "Chut darga" (descending a level). In other words, the chatan need not fear "chut darga," provided that the essential matters—that is to say, Yiddishkeit, yiras shamayim, and good middos—are as they should be.

With blessings for good tidings and a happy Purim,

## 970

[970](#_ftn_447)

By the Grace of G-d, Shushan Purim, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the annual banquet of the Ladies Auxiliary of Brownsville and East New York for the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Temimim," and to all participants,

May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

I send my greetings and blessing to all the participants in this annual banquet. May the Ribono shel Olam grant that this endeavor be met with great success in every respect.

Standing under the impression of the days of Purim, the participants will surely recall the special role that a Jewish woman—Esther—played in the miracle of Purim. This is also underscored by the fact that [the](#_ftn_448) Megillah is called **Megillas Esther**, and also [the](#_ftn_449) fast before Purim is called **Taanis Esther**.

Reflecting on the matter of **Taanis Esther**, it is of special significance that the fast which Mordechai decreed upon Esther’s request was different from all other fasts. Other fasts are incumbent upon men and women who are obligated in mitzvos, but Taanis Esther included children as well—and not only children who had reached the age of chinuch to fast, for whom it is sufficient to fast for a few hours, but even small children. They, too, fasted for three days and three nights, together with the adults (Midrash Rabbah, Esther 9:4).

This shows that there are times and matters that demand that one exert oneself even for very young children, and with full strength and to the fullest extent.

And if someone should think, "How is it appropriate for me to occupy myself with very young children and their affairs?" our Sages of blessed memory [tell](#_ftn_450) us that Mordechai—who was one of the highest royal officials, among the first in the royal palace, and, above all, one [of](#_ftn_451) the heads of the Sanhedrin—personally occupied himself with the young children. They, too, were among the fasters who went with mesiras nefesh, and through them came the Divine salvation for the entire Jewish people.

From all this, one can understand the exceedingly great merit of **all those who dedicate themselves to helping the Lubavitcher Yeshivos "Tomchei Temimim" to educate children in the aforementioned spirit.**

May this merit stand by everyone to be blessed in everything they need, and especially with much Yiddishe nachas from children and grandchildren, may they live and be well.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9771

[9771](#_ftn_452)

B”H, Shushan Purim, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, occupied with the needs of the community, etc., [Rabbi](#_ftn_453) Yechezkel, may he live and be well,

Peace and blessing!

I am writing to acknowledge receipt of your letter and its enclosure. After asking for your forgiveness, I must write my response as it stands: upon receiving your letter, I was astonished by its tone, and even more so by what was implied between the lines—as if a great salvation and deliverance had occurred at this time because an agreement was reached, etc.

After seeing that such reports are also being publicized in the press in the name of the Agudah, and with such emphasis, my sorrow was added to my astonishment. For even if you were to say that by doing so they would enhance the reputation of the Agudah, it is certainly absolutely forbidden to do so at the expense of causing harm to the chinuch of the sons and daughters of Yisrael.

This is especially true since the aforementioned "enhancement" is highly questionable; for in the end, the situation and the content of the so-called achievements will become clear, and it is understood how the aforementioned publications will be interpreted—and to the wise, a word is sufficient.

It is unnecessary to add that when I received the report regarding the "reception" and the reactions on [Beekman Street](#_ftn_454) from the shaliach who arrived from Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—who described the situation as it truly is, my astonishment and sorrow grew even greater.

May it be the will of Hashem that, finally, it will be revealed just as it was in those days at this time: "Light" —this refers to Torah, etc., and "light" etc., in its literal sense, [for the children](#_ftn_457) of Yisrael in all their dwelling places, and especially in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established.

With respect and blessing, and for good tidings eventually.

P.S.
I delayed sending this letter for several days because I was waiting for further information from there. To my great sorrow and regret, the additional information confirmed the reports regarding the "achievements" and the threatening situation. An additional detail is that the Agudah activists in Eretz Yisrael—may it be rebuilt and established—were informed of the situation in all its details; naturally, it is also distressing that the notification to them had to come through others, even though, on the face of it, this should have been their own responsibility, and their primary responsibility at that.

It is obvious that there is no desire whatsoever in anything written here to conduct a dispute with anyone or to disparage anyone’s honor; rather, perhaps this might at least be of some benefit for the future.

## 9712

B"H, 18 Adar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the honorable Rabbi, pious and G-d-fearing, engaged in communal needs, man of many deeds and fine character, etc., Rabbi Eliezer Ze'ev, may he live, known as Dr. Kirzner, Chief Rabbi, London.

Peace and blessing!

From time to time, I receive regards from you through anash in your country, and I hear of your kind interest and sympathetic attitude toward their work in spreading Torah and Yiddishkeit. I was especially pleased to hear of your public statement in support of the Mivtza Tefillin campaign—a project of great value and vast scope that has found a true echo among our fellow Jews everywhere. For the heart of the Jewish people is awake to Torah and mitzvos, especially the mitzvah of tefillin, to which the entire Torah is compared. Furthermore, it is one of the first mitzvos that the Jewish people were commanded to observe while still in the land of Egypt.

Although you do not require thanks for such a matter—for the reward of a mitzvah is the mitzvah itself—I wish to express the great satisfaction I felt regarding your support for this lofty endeavor. This is especially true when considering your high position as Chief Rabbi, which Divine Providence has placed upon you, granting you the merit of tremendous influence so that your words are heard and achieve their intended effect.

It is surely known to you that this Mivtza Tefillin has seen blessing and success from its inception; it continues to grow and expand, bearing fruit and the fruit of fruit. As our Sages of blessed memory stated in their Mishnah, "one mitzvah leads to another." If this is true for every mitzvah, how much more so for the mitzvah of tefillin, which is a foundational element in the daily life of our people, the Jewish nation, especially in these days. As it is brought in Midrash Tehillim on the verse, "But his delight is in the Torah of Hashem, and in His Torah he meditates day and night": The Jewish people said before the Ribono shel Olam, "Master of the Universe, we wish to toil in Torah day and night, but we do not have the time." The Holy One, blessed be He, said to them, "Observe the mitzvah of tefillin, and I will account it to you as if you were toiling in Torah day and night."

As we emerge from the days of Purim, and in our custom to "connect one redemption to another," may it be the will of Hashem that we all merit, together, the true and complete redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, very soon.

With respect and blessing.

## 9796

[9796](#_ftn_479)

[From the notes of Adar 5728]

On the face of it, there is a contradiction from Yoma (86a) regarding the verse "I will heal their backsliding" — that a portion of His Name rests upon them (Rashi, ad loc.). One could say that there, it refers to healing from Above that comes through *teshuvah* from *yirah*, which in any event does not transcend the *sefirah* of *Binah*. This is in contrast to here, where "For I am Hashem your Healer" refers to *Arich* (see *Or HaTorah* by the Tzemach Tzedek, *Beshalach*, p. 584; and see *Ya'ir Nativ*, p. 124). On the other hand, even regarding healing where a human hand (a doctor) is involved, there are matters "that are healed, yet not within the category of healing that is (only) from this point forward (where, consequently, a *reshimu* remains), but rather the reality itself [is transformed], etc." Or, the action of the human is merely a "category of trial" (*Responsa Tzafnas Paneach*, sec. 67; *Tzafnas Paneach* on Rambam, *Hilchos Issurei Biah*, ch. 15, law 5), and no *reshimu* remains whatsoever; a complete and total healing.

Secretary

When the attitude toward a shidduch proposal is unclear, one of the pieces of advice for gaining clarity is to pause the meetings and correspondence for a period of time and observe how this affects one's attitude, feelings, etc.

## 978

[978](#_ftn_484)

B"H, 2 Nissan, the Hillula of the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e., 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Anash—and the Temimim in particular—who are in Eretz Yisrael [Eretz](#_ftn_485)—the land upon which the eyes of Hashem are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year—may Hashem grant them life,

Peace and blessing!

In connection with the liberation of the shul and Beis Medrash founded by the Rebbe, the Tzemach Tzedek, in Jerusalem, the walled city.

This is a communal asset, a possession of all Anash wherever they may be, and their share in Jerusalem, the holy city.

A [great house](#_ftn_487), [in accordance with the two interpretations of Chazal](#_ftn_488): a place where prayer is cultivated, and a place where Torah is cultivated (the general study of Torah by the masses, and specifically in the teachings of the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek—both in Nigleh and Chassidus).

I wish to propose [establishing](#_ftn_489) an administrative committee consisting of representatives from all of Anash, the Temimim, and Chabad institutions in Eretz Yisrael, and in Jerusalem in particular:

A representative of Kolel Chabad in Eretz Yisrael, which was founded by the Alter Rebbe;

A representative of the Yishuv of Anash that was in the holy city of Hebron—founded by the Mitteler Rebbe—and the Yeshiva therein, Yeshivas Toras Emes, which for known reasons relocated and is now situated in Jerusalem—to be appointed by the administration of Toras Emes;

A representative of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, which was founded by the Rebbe (Rashab) n.e.;

A representative of Kfar Chabad, which was founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

A representative of Agudas Chabad, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and Agudas N'shei U'Bnos Chabad.

Certainly, this administrative committee will proceed immediately with the greatest possible dispatch to perfect the structure of the aforementioned shul and Beis Medrash in all its details.

May it be Hashem’s will that blessing and success rest upon this most exalted endeavor, and may the house be great in every respect—both materially and spiritually.

And the prayers of the Bnei Yisrael wherever they may be,

Which—[in the words](#_ftn_490) of the Alter Rebbe: one’s face should be toward Jerusalem, [as it is said](#_ftn_491), "And they shall pray to Hashem toward the city that You have chosen," and one should also direct their intent toward the Beis Hamikdash and toward the Holy of Holies,

And their study of the Torah of Hashem, Nigleh and Chassidus—[study](#_ftn_492) that leads to action, the performance of mitzvos with hiddur—

Will surely hasten the fulfillment of the [promise](#_ftn_493) that "Judah shall be saved and Israel shall dwell securely." [And in the words of the verse and the explanation of Chazal](#_ftn_494)—"Hashem shall establish the House of Hashem," this is the Beis Hamikdash, "and the House of the King," these are the King’s palaces—this is Melech HaMoshiach, who will come and redeem us with the true and complete Geulah, very soon.

With respect and with a blessing for great success in all the above, with joy and goodness of heart, and for good tidings regarding all the above,

M. Schneerson

To expedite the matter, and since it is difficult at this time to convene a joint meeting of Agudas Chabad, Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, and N'shei U'Bnos Chabad, surely all will agree that their representative on the aforementioned committee shall be the esteemed Rabbi Avraham Paris.

Surely, they will promptly announce the contents of this letter—regarding the establishment of the committee and its activity in the aforementioned direction—[and in the words of](#_ftn_495) our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe, with "wondrous alacrity," to show his joy and desire to fulfill the will of his Creator and to bring satisfaction to his Maker.

For the establishment of a shul and Beis Medrash anywhere is certainly the desire and will of our Creator, our Father in Heaven, and especially to restore the ruins of the shul and Beis Medrash founded by the Rebbe the Tzemach Tzedek in Jerusalem, the holy city.

Enclosed is the participation of Anash who are abroad, including my own participation, in the aforementioned activity and work.

## 9782

9782

By the Grace of G-d, 11 Nissan, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel everywhere,
May Hashem grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

Every matter in Torah, even a detail, and certainly a detail of such a comprehensive subject as *Yetzias Mitzrayim* (the Exodus from Egypt), carries a special significance and specific instructions.

The Torah tells us that before the Jews left Egypt, Hashem gave them various *mitzvos*: some they were required to fulfill while still in Egypt, and others they were to fulfill later.

Among the *mitzvos* that were commanded in Egypt, there is one that stands out because it was designated as a special *os*—a sign and a reminder—of the entire concept of *Yetzias Mitzrayim*, and was intended to serve as such not only at a specific time of year, but on all the weekdays of the entire year.

This is the *mitzvah* of *Tefillin*.

From this, it is understood that the connection between the *mitzvah* of *Tefillin* and *Yetzias Mitzrayim* is extremely broad and deep. And even in comparison to *Chag HaPesach* with all its details—those are only during the days of *Pesach*, whereas the remembrance and experience of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* must be daily, and this is marked **"as a sign upon your hand and as a memorial between your eyes"**—in the (*all* weekdays of the entire year) *Tefillin*.

* * *

Like all matters of Torah and *mitzvos*, the special significance of the *mitzvah* of *Tefillin* has many explanations, and I would like to focus here on one of them.

The concept of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* was the liberation from enslavement, beginning with the simple sense of the word—from physical forced labor (*avodas parech*), to the deepest sense of **spiritual** liberation, liberation from "Mitzrayim" (*meitzarim u'gvulim*—limitations and boundaries)—from all the constraints and restrictions that stifle the *neshamah*; until the **essential being** (*etzem mahus*) of the Jew is revealed, both as an individual and as a people.

For the essential being of a Jew is, as Hashem says: **"You are children to Hashem your G-d"**—which implies not only the *neshamah* as it is before it descends into this world, but also a Jew as he is in *Olam HaZeh*, a *neshamah* with a body and all their respective characteristics.

* * *

The concept of **"children to the Omnipresent"** (*Banim LaMakom*) means, among other things, that just as Hashem is a Ruler and Sovereign over the world and everything in it, so too must a Jew—in all matters connected to his being a **Jew**, with *Yiddishkeit*—be a ruler over the world, and not only on "Yom Tov occasions," but also in his daily life. This must be *b'fo'al mamash*—actual and in a revealed form. This means that not only should a Jew not be affected or influenced by the world around him, but on the contrary, he must rule and hold sway—in everything that pertains to *Yiddishkeit*—over all matters of the world.

Here, a simple and powerful question immediately arises: How can this be demanded of **every** Jew, and how can he achieve it?

The answer is also a simple one: Since he is a child of Hashem, Hashem has given him special **G-dly and supernatural powers—**

For this is seen even in the analogy of children and parents, where children inherit, in a natural way, the characteristics and personality traits of their parents, and parents pass this on to their children. In the *nimshal*—as Jews are **"children to the Omnipresent"**—this is in an even deeper form. As the Alter Rebbe, *Baal HaTanya v'HaShulchan Aruch*, explains, in the analogy of parents and children, the children are a reality unto themselves, only closely and deeply connected to their parents; in the *nimshal*, however—as Jews are **"children to the Omnipresent"**—Jews are always, and through Torah and *mitzvos* also in a revealed form, not a reality unto themselves, but entirely *batel* (nullified) to Hashem—their entire reality is to carry out Hashem’s will—*k'eved u'k'ven* (like a servant and like a child).

For *Yetzias Mitzrayim* also brought out and revealed: **"For the children of Israel are servants to Me; they are My servants whom I brought out of the land of Egypt."**

When a Jew brings out these G-dly powers to their fullest extent, until they permeate his entire being—not only his actions, but also his speech and thought—this gives him the ability to be a ruler and sovereign over all matters of the world around him.

* * *

And this is the concept of the *mitzvah* of *Tefillin*, as it is explained in many places, reaching its clearest and most concentrated form in the *Shulchan Aruch*:

That when a Jew puts on *Tefillin*, he must intend that Hashem commanded us to place *Tefillin* on the hand opposite the heart, and on the head opposite the brain, "so that we remember the miracles and wonders that He performed **with us**... and that He has the power and sovereignty to do in the upper and lower worlds as He wishes," and **"to subjugate to the Holy One, blessed be He, the *neshamah* which is in the brain, and also the desires and thoughts of his heart, to His service, blessed be He."** For the brain (intellect) and heart (emotion) direct all the actions, speech, and thoughts of a person. And at that time, it is indeed—*eved melech k'melech* (the king's servant is [has the power of] the king).

Thus, through being both a servant and a child of the King, the power and sovereignty "to do in the upper and lower worlds as He wishes" is carried out *b'fo'al*—beyond all limitations, *Yetzias Mitzrayim* in its fullest measure.

* * *

May Hashem grant that through fulfilling the concept of *Yetzias Mitzrayim* during *Chag HaPesach* and on all the days of the entire year, as mentioned above, we should merit the true and complete liberation from the current *galus*, the *galus* of the body and the *galus* of the *neshamah*, with kindness and mercy, in tranquility through *Moshiach Tzidkeinu* immediately.

With blessings for a *Chag HaPesach Kasher v'Sameach*,

Menachem Schneerson

## 9,787

9,787

B"H, 8 Iyar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Nissan, in addition to the telephone response,

As is the custom in Israel when the peace between a husband and wife requires strengthening and improvement, both parties should present their claims before the rabbi of the community or a local rabbi and follow his instruction according to the opinion of our Torah, the Torah of life.

It is understood that there must be good will on the part of both sides—that is, both the wife and the husband—to strengthen the peace, for [peace](#_ftn_544) is the vessel for the blessing of the Holy One, Blessed be He, in all that is needed. [And there](#_ftn_545) is nothing that can stand before the will.

Based on the above, it is understood that you should conduct yourself according to the custom of virtuous women in Israel, each of whom is called the ["pillar](#_ftn_546) of the home," regarding mitzvos in general and the mitzvos incumbent upon a woman in particular.

It is appropriate to have the mezuzos in the home checked if they have not been checked in the last twelve months. And surely you know and observe the [good custom](#_ftn_547) of setting aside a coin for tzedakah before lighting the candles on the eves of Shabbos and Yomim Tovim.

Among the advised suggestions to strengthen the feeling of bitachon, should it require strengthening, is to [recite](#_ftn_548) Psalm 23 in the Book of Tehillim—that is, the Psalm of David, "Hashem is my shepherd, I shall not lack," etc.

With blessings that Hashem fulfill the requests of your heart for the good and that you bring good tidings,

On behalf of the Rebbe, shlita,
Secretary
