## 890

890

B”H, 15 Iyar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, and involved in communal affairs,
[Rabbi](#_ftn_555) Schneur Zalman, may he live.

Shalom u’vracha!

It was with great astonishment that I read in your letter various strange notions regarding the elections for the Kfar Chabad committee—to such an extent that I was in doubt whether to respond at all, for a response grants a reality to the question, even when the response is in the negative. This is one of the reasons for the delay in my reply until now.

Nevertheless, having seen the enthusiasm regarding the [question](#_ftn_556) of language, the concern arose: who knows to what dimensions the differences of opinion regarding the aforementioned elections might reach? Therefore, I have come to write, albeit briefly:

1) The notion of holding separate elections for the various circles of Kfar Chabad residents.

How strange this notion is can be understood from the reality itself—it would be a novelty, for until now I have not heard of any settlement in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) or abroad that operates in this manner. Moreover, there are many circles within the Jewish people residing in Eretz Yisrael, yet they do not hold elections according to the number of parties and circles.

Since our Sages of blessed memory [said](#_ftn_557) that "we have not heard" is not proof, and it is possible that one might find some corner where they conduct themselves according to the aforementioned notion, regarding Kfar Chabad—there is no end to the matter. For there are circles that disagree with one another due to affiliation with this synagogue or that, the same circles you write about—Sephardim and Ashkenazim, those who advocate for study in Lashon HaKodesh or for study in Yiddish, etc., etc.

2) The notion that for every matter they should provide an accounting in general assemblies, or at least for a certain type of matter. As above, I have not heard of such a thing. Furthermore, even though the claim is just—that matters must be accounted for and a report provided—this is the role of the audit committee, not to debate matters, even important ones, specifically in public assemblies. *V’kal l’havin* (and it is easy to understand).

3) Enclosed is a copy of [my letter](#_ftn_558) to the administration of the Talmud Torah and to the parents, from which it is understood that [(in the style](#_ftn_559) of our Sages of blessed memory, there is a place that breeds lovers of peace and there is a place that breeds pursuers of peace, etc.). It is understood that in every single place, there must be extra caution regarding the character of that place.

To my greatest regret, regarding Kfar Chabad—which this year has reached [the age](#_ftn_560) of twenty—I have not yet been privileged to hear news of a drawing together of hearts, or at least that the situation is not deteriorating. Instead, news is received daily that further division has been added regarding such-and-such a matter; a dispute begins regarding a certain issue, and immediately the residents divide into two sides, or three sides, or more. Naturally, the men and women are drawn into this together, and sometimes the boys and girls as well, and the results are understood. And if this is so in ordinary times, how much more so as elections approach and are imminent.

May it be the will of the Almighty that from within itself, the father should cast the [axe](#_ftn_561)—my intention is that the same enthusiasm and *koch* (intensity) that in previous years, in other settlements, and in certain parties were used for the division of hearts **etc.** **etc.**—should be used to channel the energies that arise at such a time, and that *koch* and enthusiasm, toward the war against the *yetzer*, and that everyone should cooperate for the expansion of Kfar Chabad, both materially and spiritually. There are so many areas in which the village could have expanded **many times over** had they been attended to as they should be, yet for now, no one is paying attention to this. Instead, they "pounce" on a matter that so-and-so has been working on, is working on, and is succeeding in, etc., and consequently, one "must" find faults and shortcomings in his work and his methods, etc., etc. If one truly and sincerely wishes to bring improvements to the village, every single resident of the village will find a **vast** field to act in the affairs of the village, to establish it and expand it in quantity and quality, in which he could accomplish great and wondrous things. For in Kfar Chabad, Hashem has commanded the blessing through its founder, my father-in-law, the Rebbe, who, [as](#_ftn_563) he stood and served before, so he stands and serves even now. And with the **greatest** force, he demanded and insisted, emphatically and with the greatest strength, that all of *Anash* should be [as one man,](#_ftn_564) friends, etc., etc.

4) Since regarding every matter our Sages of blessed memory have said (Zohar Vol. III, 161b and elsewhere) that just as the Holy One, blessed be He, looked into the Torah and created the world, so too a person engages in Torah and repairs the world, it is fitting that they establish study in all the synagogues in Kfar Chabad—and that those who participate in this study should, obviously, be those who stand at the head of the sides divided against one another, as well as all those who follow in their footsteps. The study should be relevant to the matter at hand: the [Kuntres](#_ftn_565) **Hechalotzu**, which is certainly available, as it was [printed](#_ftn_566) here with the addition of the *maamar* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, on this subject. If there is a need, they can print it immediately (via photostat) from the *kuntres* that was printed previously, provided that they begin studying it as soon as possible—a study *aliba d’nafsha* (for one’s own soul), a [study](#_ftn_567) that leads to action, so that all the aforementioned and all the residents of Kfar Chabad will "arm themselves" to take [Hashem’s vengeance](#_ftn_568) **on Midian**, [as explained](#_ftn_569) by our Rebbe the Alter Rebbe on this, and by the Rebbes of Chabad, his successors, up to the Nasi of our generation, my father-in-law, the Rebbe.

And if you will say, this is also a matter of Lag B'Omer, on which [ceased](#_ftn_570) the conduct of before, when they did not show respect to one another, and it is the [day](#_ftn_571) of the rejoicing of the Rashbi, who [unites](#_ftn_572) the inner dimension of Torah with the revealed dimension of Torah. And the teaching of the Baal Shem Tov is well known, which the Tzemach Tzedek transmitted on Lag B'Omer (around the year 5604): "I want to make of Jews that they should give the harvest that the Almighty's—B"H—'desirable land' can give" (*Hayom Yom*, 17 Iyar).

With blessings for good tidings regarding the above and soon,

M. Schneerson

951

15 Iyar, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the representatives of the parents of the students of the Talmud Torah in Kfar Chabad, in the Holy Land—may it be rebuilt speedily by Mashiach Tzidkeinu—may they live:

Shalom u’Bracha!

I acknowledge receipt of your letters and the point they raise—the question of the language in which the students of the Talmud Torah should be taught.

As per my response in our telephone conversation, my opinion is that since the primary purpose of the Talmud Torah is to educate the students in the fear and love of Hashem and to teach them the Torah of Hashem and His mitzvos—which are longer than the earth and broader than the sea—and because our Sages have warned us so strongly against causing any interruption to the learning of children, to the extent that they forbade it even for the building of the Beis Hamikdash, it is understood from the above that the language in which the students are taught is not the main point. Rather, the essential points are efficiency and an increase in both quantity and quality in the knowledge of Torah and mitzvos.

[It is also understood that in a place where the language of instruction has an influence on matters of yiras shamayim and the like, then the determination of the language carries importance accordingly.]

2) It is also understood that it is not appropriate to change the language of instruction in the middle of the school year for many reasons [assuming there is no absolute necessity to make the change].

3) Under certain conditions, when parents wish to determine the language of instruction—and provided the aforementioned condition is met, that it has no bearing on yiras shamayim or matters of Shulchan Aruch, etc.—then one should not force the language of instruction upon the parents. Instead, one should explain the matter to them if their arguments are not correct. As in similar matters, the language of instruction should be determined according to the opinion of the majority of the parents, for one must follow the majority.

4) A specific point regarding Kfar Chabad: to my great regret, people "seize the opportunity" to turn every matter into a source of contention and division of hearts. This is the craft of the Yetzer Hara, to cloak every issue in the guise of yiras shamayim, etc. As is apparent from the tone of the letters from the administration and the parents, this has occurred in the present case. Therefore, it is worthwhile to conduct a search by the light of the candle—the candle of Hashem is the soul of man—to determine the true motives of each of those taking part in this new dispute.

The conclusion from all the above is that even in the telephone conversation, it was not implied that there is a desire to change things immediately. As mentioned, it is not appropriate to do so in the middle of the school year. Since there is still time until the beginning of the next school year to engage in cheshbon hanefesh and so on, the entire issue should be discussed again closer to the start of the next school year—a discussion based on the point regarding the purpose of the Talmud Torah as mentioned above.

Regarding the mention of special merits concerning the Yiddish language, it requires study whether the acquisition of these merits is the responsibility of the Talmud Torah or the obligation of the parents and the atmosphere in the home, and the wise will understand.

And finally, the main point follows:

It is a great wonder that there is no mention at all of a fundamental matter regarding the students of the Talmud Torah. From several sources, I have received unfavorable reports, etc., regarding the conduct of the students of the Talmud Torah, especially on Shabbos Kodesh and Yom Tov, and also on Erev Shabbos and Yom Tov. The same applies to their conduct in the shul, even on weekdays. Although part of the responsibility for this lies with the teachers and instructors of the Talmud Torah—for education according to Torah also pertains to their conduct outside the walls of the Talmud Torah, and especially in a holy place like the shul and the beis medrash—a significant part, and perhaps the primary part, is the responsibility of the parents, the father and the mother. It is their duty to instill good character traits in their children by all means at their disposal, and even if they are busy with other matters, this remains their primary obligation. If this is true during the school days, it is all the more so on Erev Shabbos and Yom Tov after midday, and on Shabbos and Yom Tov, when the primary responsibility rests with the parents.

Since every single matter must be utilized for the sake of Torah and yiras shamayim, my hope is strong that the enthusiasm and the *koch* that has been aroused regarding the language of instruction—which, as mentioned, is only relevant to implement close to the start of the school year—will certainly be utilized to the greatest extent for guiding the students in good character traits and matters of yiras shamayim that do not fall within the scope of the Talmud Torah curriculum, such as reciting blessings, proper tefillah, honoring parents, teachers, and elders, and also polite behavior between one another (this being one of the special lessons of the days of Sefirah: to show this respect to one another).

Immediately upon receiving this letter, you should gather for a meeting of all the parents—Ashkenazim and Sephardim, those who favor one language or another, etc.—and discuss the aforementioned issue: the conduct of the students of the Talmud Torah. In addition, discuss their conduct within the Talmud Torah regarding maintaining the order of study, discipline, etc. Discuss this with the appropriate gravity—a discussion that leads to action. Immediately on the spot, choose a committee of parents who will be responsible for the aforementioned conduct from now on. They shall appoint a number of parents who will supervise the students with a watchful eye, etc., and other matters suitable for rectifying the situation as soon as possible, and for improvement that is ever-increasing and ever-better.

May it be the will of Hashem that I receive good news regarding all the above in the return mail, and regarding the inner point that hearts have been brought closer in a true closeness, and that each of them, and all of them together, do everything in their power so that it will be fulfilled in the students of the Talmud Torah—among the rest of the students of the institutions in Kfar Chabad—that all who see them (at home and outside, on weekdays, Shabbos, and Yom Tov) will recognize them as the seed which Hashem has blessed.

This is in accordance with the will of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the founder of Kfar Chabad, as he expressed and demanded many times.

With blessings for good news regarding all the above, soon,

M. Schneerson

## 9494

Beyond the fact that the entire nation of Hashem is a [kingdom](#_ftn_586) of Kohanim and a holy nation, the Kohanim were given specific additional roles and strengths.

It gave me pleasure to read in your letter about your participation in meetings, farbrengens, shiurim, etc. My hope is strong that you utilize these shiurim and studies in a way that the [study](#_ftn_587) will lead to action, in accordance with the [instruction of our Sages, of blessed memory](#_ftn_588), that "action is the essential thing."

Indeed, there is a special role for the daughters of Israel [during these days](#_ftn_589) of Sefirah, which are a preparation for the receiving of the Torah. This is based on [what is recounted in our Torah](#_ftn_590)—the Torah of life, which provides instruction in life for all generations, for the [Torah](#_ftn_591) is eternal. Before the giving of the Torah, the Holy One, blessed be He, said to Moshe: "Thus shall you say to the House of Yaakov (and afterwards) and tell to the Children of Israel." This means that the women and daughters of Israel ("the House of Yaakov") preceded [the men] in the preparations for receiving the Torah.

## 995

[995](#_ftn_592)

By the Grace of Hashem, Days of Sefira, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner
for the educational institution "Oholei Torah"
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Shalom u’vracha!

These current days of Sefira are especially auspicious and **well-suited for the annual undertaking of the educational institution "Oholei Torah."**

It is known to all that the days of [Sefira](#_ftn_593) are a time of preparation for Kabbalas HaTorah. These days remind us of that time when the Jewish people first counted the days and weeks from their liberation from Mitzrayim until Matan Torah at Har Sinai. With each day that they counted so impatiently and with such yearning, they drew ever closer to Sinai—not only in physical distance, but spiritually as well. And when they finally reached Har Sinai, they had already completely freed themselves from all the undesirable influences and habits that had clung to them throughout **their long exile in Mitzrayim. Yet, they still did not receive the holy Torah immediately—not until they offered the [children](#_ftn_594) as "guarantors" that the Torah would be eternally guarded and cherished.**

Thus, it is emphasized every year at this time that it is not enough for the adults themselves to prepare and strengthen their connection to Torah and mitzvos. It is necessary to ensure that the **children** will be able to fulfill their task as the **Torah-guarantors**—that they be given the opportunity to learn Torah, to cherish the Torah, and, most importantly, to be imbued with Torah and mitzvos as the foundation of their daily lives.

The educational institution "Oholei Torah" has earned a distinguished place in the field of Torah education *al taharas hakodesh*. The institution deserves the fullest support of everyone who understands that **Torah and mitzvos are "our life and the length of our days"—our entire life and being.**

It is to be hoped that the hisorerus and preparations of these Sefira days will express themselves in full measure and in a tangible way—through generous support to enable the educational institution to continue and expand its educational activities, in order to create more and more "Torah-guarantors."

May the zechus of supporting and upholding the Torah stand by each and every one of you to be blessed with all the blessings, both material and spiritual, which have been promised in the holy Torah: [It](#_ftn_596) is a tree of life to those who grasp it, and those who support it are rendered happy.

With respect and blessing for success,

M. Schneerson

## 9496

[9496](#_ftn_597)

By the grace of Hashem, during the days of Sefirah, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Thirteenth Annual Convention
of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad
May Hashem grant them life

Greetings and blessings!

This year’s annual convention takes place during the auspicious days connected to Shabbos Mevarchim Chodesh Sivan, the third month, the month of Matan Torah.

The [Torah](#_ftn_598) tells us that on Rosh Chodesh Sivan, the Jewish people arrived at Mount Sinai and attained the level of **achdus** (unity). This is indicated by the words **"Vayichan sham Yisrael"** (in the singular form)—the Jewish people encamped there as one, united and unified by the resolve to accept the Torah and mitzvos.

The significance of this moment is clear from the [teaching of our Sages](#_ftn_599) that this unity of the Jewish people was the prerequisite for Matan Torah.

It has been emphasized many times that there are vital moments for Klal Yisrael, especially regarding matters of Torah and Yiddishkeit, where the woman occupies a most important place. One of these is the matter of **achdus** in the family, for it is the woman who holds the primary keys to unity between parents and children, between the parents themselves, and among the children. In this area, as is clearly evident, the woman and mother has a great deal to say—in most cases, even more than the husband and father. This is one of the reasons why the [woman](#_ftn_600) is called the "Akeres HaBayis" (the mainstay of the home).

It is also clear that the matter of achdus among Jews in a broader sense—the unity of one family with another, and the unity of the entire Jewish people as a whole—is dependent upon the achdus within the family. Where, Heaven forbid, there is a lack of unity in a family, one cannot expect unity between that family and another.

However, even when the achdus in the family is at its best, there remains the problem of achdus among Jews in general, for the foundation of true Jewish achdus is, as noted above, Torah and mitzvos.

If in all times it was not easy to achieve achdus, this problem has become far more complex in these days of "freedom" in the "free" countries, where people are not restricted as they once were regarding their place of residence, occupation, educational institutions, opinions, outlooks, and so on.

All these diversities and fragmentations—geographic, social, cultural, etc.—are the "by-products" of modern-day "freedom." These newly created circumstances have generated new problems and difficulties, which must, however, be viewed as **challenges**. With an appropriate approach and firm resolve, they can be solved.

I hope that this year’s convention of N'shei U’Bnos Chabad will dedicate the necessary attention to these mentioned problems and their solutions, without underestimating the multifaceted duties and far-reaching possibilities of Jewish women in general, and of N'shei **U’Bnos Chabad in particular. For it is certain that the duties which **Divine Providence** imposes are [never](#_ftn_601) beyond the strengths and capabilities that Divine Providence provides to carry them out in practice.

The main thing is that the convention should lead to increased and expanded activities, for **maaseh hu ha'ikar** (action is the essential thing), and may the Almighty help that you should act and accomplish to the fullest extent, according to the fullest possibilities, and with joy and goodness of heart.

With blessings for success and for good tidings in both spiritual and material matters alike.

M. Schneerson

## 9497

9497

B"H, during the days of Sefirah, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduating students of "Beis Rivkah"
in Montreal
May Hashem keep them alive

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding your upcoming graduation. May it be the will of Hashem that it take place at a favorable and auspicious time, and may your inner desires to be true daughters of Chabad and daughters of Israel be fulfilled.

As students of "Beis Rivkah," you surely know how to appreciate the special merit of a daughter of Israel—a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah—and of a daughter of Chabad in particular; the merit that is connected to your future as the *akeres habayis*.

In these times, and under current circumstances, many responsibilities in connection with the management of the home, the spiritual state of the Jewish home, the education of children, and so on, have shifted to a significant extent from the *baal habayis* to the *akeres habayis*. This means that Jewish daughters must receive a much broader and deeper preparation than in previous generations.

You have been privileged to learn and prepare yourselves at "Beis Rivkah," where you receive the desired preparation for life. However, the success of this depends to a great extent on you yourselves, the students: on your firm will, your *hasmadah* and *shekidah*, and your good conduct. May Hashem Yisbarach grant you success, that you should grow in all of this and go *meichayil el chayil* —from good to better—and may you be an inexhaustible source of true Jewish, Chassidic *nachas* for your parents, your educators, and all of Klal Yisrael.

With blessings for success and for good tidings.

## 9,398

9,398

B"H, 23rd of Matmonim, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the fourth day of Parshas Shemini—and I ask your forgiveness for the delay in responding due to the press of many matters—

In it, you write regarding the words of so-and-so concerning his daughter, etc., in connection with a proposal of honorable standing, etc.

It is a great wonder that the aforementioned individual troubled you with this, for I have **already** replied to his letter [the content of which is similar to the matters you bring], and the answer was that regarding what is written in his letter, he must speak with his daughter, *tichyeh*.

Since everything is by Divine Providence, and especially since, on the face of it, there was no place in this matter to trouble you, perhaps this opportunity has come to me to express my hope that you will continue to increase the dissemination of the *maayanos* in your holy community and in your surroundings in general—the *maayanos* of the words of the Living G-d, the Torah of the Baal Shem Tov, his students, and his students' students. As is known from the *Iggeres HaKodesh* of the author of *Toldos Yaakov Yosef* (printed in the sefer *Poras Yosef*), that when your *maayanos* spread outward, the Master, King Moshiach, will come.

And this is also related to these days, the days of *Sefirah*, and the request to be purified and to be sanctified with holiness from above, and through this, abundant bounty will be drawn down into all the worlds—*Sefirah* and preparation for the receiving of the revealed and the inner Torah together; and not merely a preparation, but the sole sign for determining the time of the giving of our Torah, "you shall count fifty days", which is not the case for the other *moadim* and *regalim*, etc.

With respect and blessing.

999

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Sivan, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Nissan Waxman
The Rabbinical Court, 33 King David St., Tel Aviv

Greetings and blessings,

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 23rd of the month, which reached me with some delay.

It is understood that I remember you, even though I do not recall if we have met in person. This is because you previously sent me the sefer *Tomer Devorah*, where the greatness of *ahavas Yisrael* is also discussed. Although I do not have that edition of yours at hand, I believe you addressed this matter in your [note] there.

As for the essence of your letter, it gave me satisfaction to see that your heart is sensitive to the situation of our Jewish brethren in the exile of India. This gives me hope that the lines below will find a proper echo in your heart. For some time now, I have been demanding and requesting, in every possible way, from the activists of *aliyah*—without entering into the essence of their work and its methods—that they should not cause the spiritual leaders of any community to abandon their congregants and relocate to any place, even to *Eretz HaKodesh*. If, at any time, the state of Yiddishkeit in every place depended on the community leaders, and especially the spiritual guides, how much more so in our generation, an orphaned generation. It is obvious, and all the more so, that it is forbidden to assist these leaders when they flee from the battlefield, and it is a *kal v’chomer* of a *kal v’chomer* that it is forbidden to conduct propaganda for them to flee from the battlefield, for they are thereby abandoning many precious Jewish souls. Unfortunately, this is not merely a hypothesis or a remote concern, for we see this tangibly in the abandonment of a city or community by its spiritual leader.

Even in a place where there are two or three spiritual leaders and the like, beyond the [statement of our Sages, of blessed memory] that two *tzaddikim* in one city are not comparable to one *tzaddik* in a city—and even regarding that, they said, "its splendor has departed, its glory has departed"—the leaders of our generation, even when several are in one place, are insufficient to provide spiritual nourishment for all those in their surroundings, even to a minimal degree, for many reasons. Would that they succeed in reaching a significant portion of them. The results are understandable when one of them leaves the place and there is no one to replace him, in addition to the fact that his colleagues are weakened in their work by his departure, and the idea creeps in among them that if such-and-such a leader abandons the battlefield, then the matter becomes permissible, and so on.

The [proverb] and the hint of our Sages, of blessed memory, is famous: "Such is the craft of the *yetzer hara*: today he says to him, 'Do this,' etc., until he says [to him, 'Go worship idols']" (*Shabbos* 105b). The beginning of the *yetzer hara’s* enticement is that he says "do this" and agrees to the conduct that preceded his enticement—namely, according to Torah and *mitzvos*. In other words, he cloaks his enticement in a mantle of holiness (*ish*). And what mantle is more beautiful in our time than *aliyah* to *Eretz HaKodesh* (may it be rebuilt and established), and a word to the wise is sufficient.

When I pleaded with several *aliyah* activists who visited me to conduct their propaganda among the guided rather than the guides, even those who promised me so at the time of our conversation, upon crossing the threshold, began specifically with propaganda among the rabbis and guides. When I asked, "How can this be?" they answered me that there is hope that [the body] follows the head, and when it is publicized in the community that their rabbi has made *aliyah* to *Eretz HaKodesh*, all the members of his community will follow him!

Surely you know, as one who is familiar with the youth and the *baalei batim* in the United States in general, how ridiculous these words are and how they lack any foundation in reality. The same applies to the Yiddishkeit of South America. Furthermore, even regarding the Yiddishkeit of Morocco, from where many *baalei batim* made *aliyah* to *Eretz HaKodesh*, their *aliyah* was not influenced at all by the rabbi’s *aliyah* before them. What the relocation of the rabbi or *chacham* did influence was a marked decline in the religious state of the community in general, and especially among the Jewish youth. This is known and famous to all those who have visited those countries in recent years and saw tangibly how the aforementioned propaganda, where it succeeded, brought about an unimaginable religious decline.

For the time being, I do not see anyone who has begun to rectify the situation, even though the possibilities for doing so exist.

It is very painful to elaborate on this matter, especially since, as mentioned, the *shluchim* are adopting this line, at least in all those countries from which I have received various reports regarding their propaganda.

It is close to certain that the same thing happened in India, at least in several important places, in the same way that this happened in several places in Morocco, South America, etc.

What is written above does not at all correspond to the gravity of the situation and the destructive nature of the aforementioned propaganda. It is especially incomprehensible, for if they had invested energy to the same extent in propaganda among the *baalei batim*, they would also have succeeded, and there would not have been a war against the religious state of those who remain—and if you will, also against the moral state of those who remain. After all, even against the Jewish people living abroad, it is forbidden to wage war by removing their spiritual leader, etc., etc.

May it be the will that each one of us, within the entirety of the Jewish people, recognizes the greatest responsibility—especially in this era of ours—toward the Jewish people in his near and far surroundings. May he do everything within his power to make it easier for them to study Torah and observe its *mitzvos*, to instill Torah and its *mitzvos* in every possible place, and to strengthen the hands of all those who are engaged in this and who lead in this in every place where Jewish people reside.

And to explain to them the [ruling of our Sages, of blessed memory] that "a student who is exiled, his teacher is exiled with him," which obligates, by a *kal v’chomer*, an absolute and categorical prohibition against inciting the rabbi and assisting him in abandoning his students and their families in the exile. There is a spiritual responsibility in this matter—*pikuach nefashot* regarding eternal life, the life of Torah and *mitzvos*. And if a doubt of *pikuach nefashot* is treated this way, how much more so when, to our great sorrow, the matter is not in the category of doubt, as stated above.

It is not my intent at all to play the devil’s advocate for anyone among the Jewish people, and all the more so for spiritual guides, but it is not acceptable to the intellect that someone should ascend spiritually, even by relocating his residence to *Eretz HaKodesh*, at the expense of the spiritual decline of many of his followers and those he influences.

Seemingly, I have written at length on this matter, but it does not at all correspond to the gravity of the situation and the danger to many precious souls in Israel. For even [one soul] of Israel is a whole world, and whoever sustains it in true life—the life of Torah and *mitzvos*—has sustained a whole world, [and from the] positive you infer the negative, etc.

With respect and blessing, in the style of my revered father-in-law, the Rebbe, for the receiving of the Torah with joy and inwardness, and may it be the will that I merit to be informed of good news that there are activists who have ceased propaganda in the aforementioned manner and are also influencing their colleagues in this direction.

## 9504

B"H, Isru Chag HaShavuos, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students graduating from the "Beis Rivkah" elementary school
in Kfar Chabad, in our Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established,
May Hashem grant you life!

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received your letter regarding your graduation from elementary school as you transition to the Beis Rivkah high school. May it be in a good and successful hour.

We have just come from the time of the Giving of our Torah, which, as is well known, gave the women and daughters of Israel a primary role. [As the Torah relates](#_ftn_631) and as our Sages of blessed memory explain, before the giving of the Torah, the Ribono shel Olam commanded Moshe Rabbeinu to first turn to the women and daughters of Israel to receive their consent, as the verse specifies: "Thus shall you say (first) to the House of Yaakov (these are the women), and tell (afterwards) to the Children of Israel (these are the men)." And certainly, the response of "We will do [and we will hear]" followed this path, with the women giving their consent first, with a whole heart and a willing soul.

Every year at this time, these matters are renewed with an added light, strength, and assistance from Above.

And if this is true in all generations, how much more so in [our generations](#_ftn_634), where, due to various reasons and the conditions of the time, many roles that were primarily the responsibility of the **baal habayis**—the husband and father—have shifted to the **akeres habayis**—the mother of the children. For this reason, a special education and special preparation for the daughters of Israel are essential. This is the role of the "Beis Rivkah" school, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory. Happy is your portion that you have merited to be students and to be educated in this lofty educational institution.

May it be the will of Hashem that what you undertake will succeed, that you will be a successful example and a model for the daughters of Israel, bringing much true nachas to your parents and teachers, may they live.

With blessings for outstanding success and for good tidings.

## 9505

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Yona Kesse 
Greetings and blessings!

After a long interval, I was pleased to receive your letter dated the 3rd of Sivan, although, of course, I have received regards from you in the meantime quite often through our friend Mr. Shlomo Maidanchik and other anash. It is understood that they tell me about the assistance you provide for the affairs of Chabad and Kfar Chabad, and that in addition to the assistance itself, you do so with a pleasant countenance. Knowing you, it is surely unnecessary to ask you to continue in this manner, and in a way that is "increasing and growing."

I felt a special joy in reading in your letter that you have once again become involved in public affairs. It is my hope that, just as we discussed here, it will be in a manner that yields maximum benefit regarding yourself and regarding the benefit of the public. For if in every place one must strive to utilize every power of influence in the best way and to the fullest extent, how much more so in our Holy Land, and all the more so in our current era—a time of upheavals, the blurring of boundaries, and the confusion of values, etc.—as we have spoken about this several times during our face-to-face conversations.

It is understood that sometimes the responsibility involved can instill awe and fear, but we have been promised that in every good and holy matter, special assistance and help is granted from the very essence of goodness and holiness—the Holy One, Blessed be He.

May it be His will that, in accordance with all that has been said, the issue about which you write at the beginning of your letter will finally be resolved in a completely satisfactory manner, and that full opportunity will be given to Kfar Chabad to fulfill its role in its immediate and distant surroundings, with peace of mind, and to utilize its ability and strengths in the phrasing of the mamme-loshn: from good to better, and even better.

With blessings that you should succeed in your activities in all that is written above, in both private and public matters, and in the affairs of Chabad, with health, a good state of mind, and good organization.

## 9506

9506

B"H, 10 Sivan, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the family of the late, renowned activist, a man of many accomplishments, a lover of Torah and one who cherished the Sages, Mr. [Yosef](#_ftn_637) a"h Bardugo,

Peace and blessing!

It was only recently that I learned of the passing of your dear father, who was involved in the needs of the community, a man of many accomplishments, a man of fine character, a scion of a distinguished lineage, Mr. Yosef, may he rest in peace. I share in your sorrow, and may Hashem, who is blessed and exalted, comfort you twofold.

Knowing the family tradition in the realm of sustaining and disseminating Yiddishkeit, my hope is strong that the members of the family, may they live, will not only continue this ancestral tradition but will even increase in it. For it is well known how much *nachas ruach* is brought to the soul by the mitzvos and good deeds of the children and relatives who keep the way of Hashem and continue the good works of the father, husband, etc., through their conduct in daily life according to the Torah and mitzvos, serving as a living example to all those in their immediate and extended surroundings.

And in all such matters, we are assured: [A person who sanctifies himself a little below is sanctified much from above](#_ftn_638).

With regards and blessing to all the members of the family, may they live, and may it be the will of Hashem that from here on you know no more sorrow, and that only goodness and kindness be your portion, in goodness that is visible and revealed.

## 9507

[9507](#_ftn_639)

B"H, Sunday, Parshas Beha'aloscha, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Women’s Association of Brownsville and East New York,
May Hashem grant you life,

Blessings and peace!

This year, the annual luncheon is being held shortly after Shabbos Parshas Beha'aloscha, and this letter, too, is written during the week associated with the parsha of "kindling the lights."

In general, there are three types of kindling lights:

The light of the Menorah in the Beis Hamikdash—a mitzvah given to Aharon and his children, the Kohanim. However, this light was kindled only for as long as the Beis Hamikdash existed.

The light of Chanukah—a mitzvah given to **all** Jews, in all times, and observed every year during the eight days of Chanukah.

**The light of Shabbos and Yom Tov—**the light that a Jewish woman kindles every Erev Shabbos and Erev Yom Tov, throughout the entire year.

The purpose of kindling these lights is to spread **"ner mitzvah v'Torah ohr"**—the illumination of Torah and mitzvos—so that the Ribono shel Olam will cause His Divine Shechinah to rest not only in the Beis Hamikdash, but in every Jewish home and in every Jewish heart.

Here, once again, the significant role that the Jewish woman occupies in illuminating the home with the light of Torah and mitzvos is underscored, ensuring the home becomes a dwelling place for the Divine Shechinah. This also highlights the importance of your work in supporting the holy Torah institutions of Lubavitch, which grants you a share in the vast and far-reaching activities of the Lubavitcher Torah institutions.

May it be Hashem’s will that this merit stand by you all, that the annual event be a great success, and that each and every one of you, together with your families—may they live—be blessed in all that you need, [from His](#_ftn_642) full, open, holy, and generous hand.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9108

9108

B"H, in the week of Parshas Beha'aloscha, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants in the annual dinner of Yeshivas Achei-Temimim in Newark
May Hashem grant them life

Peace and Blessing!

The participants in the annual dinner will surely bring with them the spirit of the parsha, **Beha'aloscha es ha'neiros** ("When you kindle the lights"), which is read this Shabbos, in honor of the celebration.

As the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya and Shulchan Aruch and founder of Chabad, explains, the concept of "kindling the Menorah" in the practical and daily life of every Jew is the kindling of the neshamah, which is likened to a Menorah and a *ner*, as it [states](#_ftn_643) **"The lamp of Hashem is the neshamah of man,"** with the light of Torah and mitzvos, for **"a mitzvah is a lamp and Torah is light."**

The Menorah had seven lamps (seven branches with oil cups), corresponding to the seven types of Jews who serve the Ribono shel Olam in seven different ways: through ahavah, yirah, Torah study, and so on, as explained at length (**Likutei Torah**, Parshas Beha'aloscha).

This underscores the obligation that lies upon every Jew: not only to kindle his own light, his own neshamah, with the light of Torah and mitzvos, and to make his own home a Mishkan and Mikdash for the Divine Shechinah, but also to help every other Jew kindle the Divine spark in their neshamah and illuminate every Jewish home, of all types, so that they too may become a fitting vessel for the Divine Shechinah, and fulfill the Ribono shel Olam's will and promise of **"And I will dwell among them"** — [resting](#_ftn_646) within each and every one of them.

Yeshivas Achei-Temimim in Newark is a *Mikdash me'at* where the neshamos of Jewish children are illuminated with the light of Torah and mitzvos. However, there are still many Jewish children, young neshamos, who still need to be kindled and illuminated. Therefore, it is of such great importance that Yeshivas Achei-Temimim in Newark should not only be able to continue its activities, but should also be able to expand its capacity to take in as many children as possible.

Great is the zechus of all the esteemed baalei-batim and friends who have a share in the support and expansion of the yeshiva. May the Ribono shel Olam bless each and every one of you in this important endeavor, as well as in your own needs, both materially and spiritually.

With respect and blessing for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9509

[9509](#_ftn_648)

B"H, the week of Parshas Beha'aloscha Es HaNeiros, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch
For the Chag HaSiyum, Montreal
May Hashem keep them alive

Shalom and Bracha!

In connection with the Chag HaSiyum in the coming week, I send my blessing to all those completing [a tractate], as well as to the Roshei Yeshiva, the administrators, the educators, and all the students, may they live.

Since on the Shabbos preceding the Siyum of this year we read Parshas **Beha'aloscha Es HaNeiros**, it certainly serves as a preparation and an awakening for those completing the Siyum and for all the participants.

This is especially true in light of what is explained in **Likutei Torah** (Parshas Beha'aloscha) by the Alter Rebbe: that the concept of the Menorah—for the soul is called a "lamp," [as it is written](#_ftn_649), "**The lamp of Hashem is the soul of man**," etc.—implies that there are in the souls of the Jewish people seven levels, which correspond to seven levels in the *avodah* of Hashem. There is one who serves out of love that is drawn like water, another out of love like flames of fire, and another through the Torah, which is the middle line, etc. (see there at length).

From this comes the directive for every single Jew: not only to continue [and raise up] their own souls—the **eternal lamp** of the **"lamp of the mitzvah and the light of Torah"**—but also to kindle and ignite the soul of every single Jew, of all types, in such a way that they and their homes will also become a dwelling place and a sanctuary for Him, may He be blessed, in accordance with the will and promise of the Holy One, Blessed be He: **"And I will dwell among them,"** [within](#_ftn_653) each and every one of them.

And if this applies to every single Jew, it applies all the more so to the *talmidei hatemimim*, whose role—in the words of the great founder of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim, the Rebbe [Rashab], may his soul rest in Eden—is to be **"lamps to illuminate,"** which is the very essence of their *shlichus*.

May it be the will that each and every one of those completing the Siyum, together with all the students of the Yeshiva, may they live, will fulfill their *shlichus* as students of Yeshivas Tomchei Temimim Lubavitch: to spread the **light of Torah**—the revealed Torah and the Torah of Chassidus, for it is one Torah for us all—and the **"lamp of the mitzvah"**—the fulfillment of *mitzvos* with vitality and beauty, for [the deed](#_ftn_655) is the essential thing—and in a manner of "increasing and going further, increasing and shining," with joy and a glad heart.

With blessings for outstanding success in both material and spiritual matters alike, and for good tidings in all that has been mentioned.

## 9511 

24 Sivan, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad in the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily,
May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

In response to the inquiry regarding the proposal to organize a trip of several weeks during the upcoming month of Tishrei for the boys who were orphaned in the war in the Holy Land, as a continuation of their Bar Mitzvah celebration,

The proposal does not seem appropriate to me at all, for the following reasons:

a) The concept of a Bar Mitzvah—when a boy becomes obligated in mitzvos—is inconsistent with the nature of a trip (vacation and entertainment). On the contrary, it could be said that they are opposites, for on this day the boy accepts upon himself the **yoke** of the Kingdom of Heaven and the **yoke** of Torah and mitzvos.

It is understood that this does not contradict the fact that this acceptance of the yoke and these obligations should be carried out with true joy and a whole heart, as the boy merits receiving a special shlichus as a son and servant of our Father in Heaven, the King of Kings, the Holy One, Blessed be He.

With this, it is also understood that despite the great joy—and as our Sages have related, that Avraham Avinu, the first Hebrew, made a great feast on the day of the Bar Mitzvah of Yitzchak Avinu (Bereishis Rabbah 53:10; see also Zohar Chadash Bereishis 10:3, 15:4)—it is the custom of Yisroel [to recite Tachanun then], etc. For as stated, the day of a Bar Mitzvah is not a time for cessation of work, etc., but on the contrary, for an increase in work—the work of Heaven, Torah and mitzvos.

b) Another point in this matter is that we are dealing with war orphans. A trip that takes these orphans away from their homes for a period of time is inappropriate, as it would further emphasize the feeling of loneliness of the widows, and in many cases, of the brothers and sisters as well. On the contrary, as the boy becomes a **gadol**, his duty toward his mother and the household in general should also grow, to do what is within his power to encourage their spirits and strengthen their trust in Hashem, the Creator and Guide of the world, who watches over each and every one with hashgacha pratis.

c) It is likely that a large portion of the mothers and families would set aside their own feelings—their longing for the boy who has traveled, etc.—only so that the boy might enjoy and take pleasure in the trip. But in my opinion, the pleasure and enjoyment are not worth the loneliness that would be further emphasized for the mother and family members. Furthermore, and this is also essential: as mentioned, the Bar Mitzvah should strengthen the boy’s sense of responsibility, since he has become a gadol for mitzvos, not exempt him from it. And all the more so, he should not begin his period of maturity with enjoyment at the expense of others' pain. And the wise will understand.

d) If this is true at all times of the year, it is certainly true for the month of Tishrei, the month of the holidays and festivals, when the place of the husband and father is felt most acutely. One must make a special effort to fill that void to the extent possible. All those for whom this matter is close to their hearts must do what is in their power so that these families, too, may celebrate the festivals in a fitting state of mind, as instructed by our Torah, the Torah of life.

e) A substitute for the aforementioned proposal—which is also consistent with the points emphasized in this letter—is to invite the Bar Mitzvah boys **together** with their mothers, etc., to Kfar Chabad for the days of the festivals and Yomim Tovim of the upcoming month of Tishrei, for all the days or a portion of them, in the same manner as was arranged during the past Pesach, and especially during the time of our rejoicing.

f) There is no contradiction in the above to the proposal to host the Bar Mitzvah boys and Bat Mitzvah girls in a summer camp in Kfar Chabad, as that is only for a short duration and in close proximity (relatively speaking) to the family, in addition to the possibility of visits, telephone conversations, etc.

With blessings for success and good tidings,

M. Schneerson

## 9414

9414

By the Grace of G-d, Erev Shabbos Parshas Ali Anu Lah, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter...

I wish to express my strong hope that during these auspicious days, the days of Geulah, 12-13 Tammuz, and the days preceding [and following] them, you will bring to mind the narrative of the [Geulah], the narrative of the imprisonment that preceded it, and the narrative of the circumstances that led to them.

This is a remembrance that leads to hisbonenus—a hisbonenus and "study" of these narratives that leads to action.

Action in practice, through activities that constitute the foundation and the inner essence of the aforementioned narratives: the dissemination of Yiddishkeit, Torah (both the revealed and the inner dimensions), and its mitzvos, even to the point of mesiras nefesh.

Mesiras nefesh (of one’s will and all one’s affairs) from a place of true expansiveness. For even in a situation where the promise "Hashem will place the fear and dread of you..." is fulfilled in its entirety, one must still remain constantly and truly fixed in his heart with the matter of his mesiras nefesh to Hashem.

To stand strong against every obstacle and hindrance, every enemy [and avenger] —both from without and from within.

And to be confident that, in the end, all obstacles and hindrances will be nullified, and the activities will succeed, going from strength to strength, increasing in light.

And the number of those who work in this—the workers of the day, making things [bright] —will grow and grow, until it is beyond counting—

Until the fulfillment of the prophecy that "the [knowledge] and wisdom [and truth] will [increase], and the earth will be [full] of the knowledge of Hashem," with our imminent, true, and complete Geulah through Moshiach Tzidkeinu.

With blessings,

**M. Schneerson**

## 9515

[9515](#_ftn_686)

B"H, Erev Shabbos Parshas Ali Be'er Anu Lah, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished Rabbi, the distinguished Chossid, G-d-fearing, learned, and engaged in communal needs, etc.,
[Rabbi](#_ftn_687) Shlomo Yosef, may he live.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the 4th of Tammuz and those preceding it.

[I express](#_ftn_688) my strong hope...

With blessings for good tidings in good health,
M. Schneerson

P.S.
Regarding the sentiments of the [report](#_ftn_689) (Rabbi M.A.), may he live, etc., to perpetuate his name, etc. — it would be best if it were in the Kollel under the auspices of Toras Emes. Regarding the advantages — his [Yiras Shamayim] and the resources at their disposal will suffice. And more.

[Regarding the comments](#_ftn_690) of your honor in your letter of the 3rd of Sivan (concerning being *b'derech rechoka* [on a distant journey] in **this** year and the like — is there a matter of being *b'derech rechoka*, as I wrote in [my notes](#_ftn_691)?), and by way of introduction — the **foundation** of my own deliberation is: since the matter concerns: 1) a subject that carries the penalty of *kares*, 2) on the other hand — that the males from the age of thirteen and up would be for several hours [b'derech rechoka] [from Yerushalayim](#_ftn_693), it is not a minor matter (and all the more so — those who are *b'derech rechoka* in any case should not force the issue to enter Yerushalayim specifically during those hours).

[My conclusion](#_ftn_694) is that there is doubt and a *sfeik sfeika* [double doubt], etc., in the case at hand, and therefore those who are *b'derech rechoka* should not ascend, and it is best that those who are inside — should leave.

— A separate discussion regarding those who have never left Yerushalayim —

And furthermore, to preface — that it is *kal v'chomer* [a fortiori] regarding *Pesach Rishon* (and with the addition — of women), as I said to those who asked me then.

And regarding the letter of your honor: 1) **First of all, from any perspective, etc.** — The answer: (as above) in *Pesach Rishon*, it is *kal v'chomer* that there is the aforementioned concern, and one who was not *b'derech rechoka* then — is liable for *kares* for intentional neglect. And nevertheless: it is **simple** that even according to the opinion that even if one was *b'derech rechoka* during *Pesach Rishon*, he is still liable for *kares* for not performing **Pesach Rishon** (when done intentionally), nevertheless, he **should not** add transgression during **Pesach Sheini** — and be intentional then as well, even though there is no practical difference regarding the *kares* **of Pesach Rishon**. 2) When one is *b'derech rechoka* during *Pesach Sheini* — he will also be exempt from *kares*, at least according to the opinion of the *Mishnah* that one who was intentional in the first and *b'derech rechoka* in the second is exempt. 3) **And the main point** — all those who were *b'derech rechoka* during *Pesach Rishon* (and among them — most of the guests) will gain everything by being *b'derech rechoka* during *Pesach Sheini* (for the aforementioned doubt).

**A tremendous question regarding all the generations, etc.** — Until after the war of last year, the hand of the nations was strong, etc.

[The precision](#_ftn_697) of "mine" in the language of the *Shas* — that the **Torah** pushed it aside, and specifically the precision regarding the matter of "because of *tumah* I pushed it aside, let him return and perform it in *tumah*" — and he raises a difficulty on this, for the *Minchas Chinuch* says that all this is not necessarily so. With all due respect to the *Minchas Chinuch*, I am not obligated to force an explanation of his words 1) in a place where there is a liability of *kares*, 2) when they are the opposite of the simple meaning in the *Shas*. And to add — that according to the distinction (**as the simple** language and matter in the *Shas*) between the pushing aside of *tumah* (and *derech rechoka*) and other forms of *ones* [duress], one can understand why in all the examples in the *Shas* it specifies **impure** people, etc., even though in many of them it could have been *ones* and the like. And we do not need to say that since in some cases they must be impure — it phrased it that way for all of them.

[My intent](#_ftn_698) in "comparing the Bavli and the Yerushalmi" is that we should not say that the **anonymous** Bavli rules against Rabbi Yehuda. And in the Yerushalmi it remains a dispute (except that one must learn from the rule of [the *Yad HaChazakah*](#_ftn_699), that many depart from this rule).

**A decided law in the Rambam, etc., the anonymity of his language, etc.** — It is known in the rules of the Rambam that he does not bring things that are learned through deduction, etc. And a greater innovation than what I wrote — see in the *Tzafnas Paneach* (collected) on the Torah, *Beha'aloscha* (regarding the community and the pushing aside of Shabbos).

**And the four cubits that are not in the *Gevul* and the Altar in *Eretz Yisrael*, etc.** — We are dealing with the opinion of Rabbi Yehuda, that in his days there was no prophet to establish the location of the Altar, etc. — and nevertheless he wanted to offer, etc. And the *Acharonim* have already elaborated on this. And this brings to mind a special pamphlet on this, *Karnot HaMizbeach* (Warsaw, 5688), which collected all the aforementioned difficulties **and the like** and resolves them (even though some of his words — require study).

And to note — (seemingly) the building of the Altar (*Hilchos Beis HaBechirah*, end of chapter 2) can be done during the time of the obligation of offering the *Korban Pesach* and there is still time to offer it.

**A simple question: Where do we find the law of *derech rechoka* in *Pesach Sheini*?**

**A simple answer**: In the *Mishnah* (*Pesachim* 95a), "What is the difference between the first *Pesach* and the second, etc." And in the Rambam (end of *Hilchos Korban Pesach*), and it is not mentioned in any place (that I have seen) to say that it was taught and omitted *derech rechoka*. And see *Tosfos* s.v. *Mah Sham*.

At the end of your honor's letter, **an apology, etc.** — This too, in my humble opinion, is simple: there is no place for this request, etc., **and on the contrary**. And similar to *Bava Metzia* (84a, bottom). And I am accustomed to explaining from our Sages (*Kiddushin* 30b), *Et Ha'av* (with an extra, *et* to include) — (**by** their beginning being in their end) in their end.

[And in many places](#_ftn_705) (everywhere?) it is found that the teaching of "do not read it as" does not negate the reading that is in the text, but rather adds to it, and both are present in the conclusion. And I have not found this in the *Talmudic Encyclopedia*.

And we conclude with a question (and entreaty) in kindness: When, finally, will the 13th, 14th volumes, etc., be published? For the good is in the abundance of each one of them, and may [the owner](#_ftn_707) not, G-d forbid, be withheld from good.

## 9516

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mrs. Shifra Yehudis, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

Your letter of 23 Nissan, which was apparently sent via regular mail, along with its enclosure, has just been received.

Many thanks for the good news regarding the most exalted activities about which you write. May it be His will that you continue to share good news in this regard, and also—and this is, of course, the main thing—true Jewish, Chassidic *nachas* from all your children, may they live.

The administration of Tzeirei Agudas Chabad surely conveyed to you the content of my letter regarding the rejection of the idea of the *bar-mitzvah* boys traveling here. I mention this matter because I am certain that you, too, participated in the aforementioned discussion.

And from one matter to another, regarding a similar subject: it is not advisable to hold *bat-mitzvah* celebrations, since the rabbis of Israel are still divided in their opinion as to whether there is a place to institute this ceremony. There are many sides to the issue, and it is still too early to establish a definitive *halacha* in this regard. On the other hand, it is appropriate to invite them to the Kfar Chabad summer camps, and the same applies to the *bar-mitzvah* boys. Without a vow, there will be a contribution from here of a *maaser* (ten percent) toward the expenses of hosting the aforementioned boys and girls at the Kfar Chabad summer camp. It would be good to inform the camp administration or those involved in this activity about this matter, along with the first check enclosed herewith as a start. Surely, at the conclusion of the camps, they will report an accurate accounting here.

With blessings for good news in all the above, and in particular for success in the education of the children, may they live,

And with the blessing of the upcoming *Chag HaGeulah*.

## 9517

9517

B"H, 8 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Rabbi Zvi Weinman

Following up on what we discussed when you were here, and what the esteemed Rabbi, the Chassid, etc., Rabbi Chaim Mordechai A. Hodakov, brought to my attention regarding your letter to him concerning Rabbi Dr. J. H.:

## 9518

[9518](#_ftn_713)

[Beginning of Tammuz, 5728]

In accordance with the severity of this strain, Rabbi Tzvi, may he live, Weinman told me that he visited Mr. Bronfman, may he live, in Montreal, and he replied that he would come to their aid with a significant sum, provided that you would agree to it. During Mr. Bronfman’s visit to the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt and established (approximately in the middle of the month of Tammuz), he will be in contact with you regarding this.

And there is no need to elaborate to one such as yourself on the magnitude of the matter and its value.

Naturally, I am very interested to know the follow-up on the matters about which you spoke with me during your visit to New York, especially since the situation from then until now has not become any quieter, but rather the opposite.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this fourth month be a month of joy and gladness in the fulfillment of the promise of the true and complete Redemption through Mashiach Tzidkeinu, immediately.

With respect and blessings.

## 9521

By the Grace of Hashem,
Days of Redemption, 12-13 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Management Committee of the Tzemach Tzedek Shul in the Old City of Jerusalem, the Holy City — may it be built and established by Mashiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days.

May they live,

Peace and Blessing!

A year and a month have already passed since the liberation of the Old City, and with it, the Shul founded according to the directive of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek. According to reports and information, it is the only one that remains in a condition suitable for both davening and Torah study, in accordance with the requirements of Halacha.

At the very first opportunity, I wrote that it must be repaired and improved, etc., as quickly and urgently as possible, in order to daven there as consistently as the security situation allows, until it becomes possible to daven there three times every day, etc.

In the time that has passed since then, certain sums have been received from various sources to enable the necessary repairs and improvements. Together with the donation and transmittal of these funds, I also expressed a strong hope that this would further accelerate the pace of the work to improve the aforementioned Shul and Beis Medrash, and increase the study of Torah there—both the revealed Torah and Chassidus, and in particular the teachings of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek.

To my **greatest** regret, and to my **greatest** astonishment no less, throughout this entire time, the reports that have arrived regarding the repair of the Shul and Beis Medrash and the progress made—as mentioned—have been both astonishing and distressing. There is no need to dwell on this alarming matter, especially since the committee members surely visit the Tzemach Tzedek Shul from time to time and see the situation on the ground.

It is understood that there is no lack of excuses and pretexts, even the claim of *ones* (circumstances beyond one's control) which the Torah exempts. But it is also understood and simple that we will not be saved by excuses, nor will the Shul be restored to its former glory through them. Even regarding a genuine *ones* which the Torah exempts, we do not say "it is considered as if it were done," and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Another point regarding the above, although in comparison to what was written above it is secondary to the secondary: At a time when many Anash and Chabad institutions are suffering from a deficit in their funds—a *defizit* in the vernacular—which prevents the development of their affairs, a significant sum is sitting in the Shul’s fund, and for many months it has remained like a stone that no one turns over. Instead, there is an ongoing debate about who is to blame for this, etc., and as mentioned, all the debates in the world will not help the progress of things in practice.

Another point, which is also perhaps secondary to the secondary, but which indicates the way things are being handled: Although it was decided that there would be a special bank account for the aforementioned matter, and that all funds would be deposited into this account, and that a separate accounting of income and expenses for this matter would be maintained, and that two people would be chosen and appointed—who would have the authority to sign checks, and specifically both together and not one alone—yet until now, **nothing** has been heard regarding the opening of the bank account, nor regarding the selection and appointment of the two signatories. As for the accounting, only one statement has been received, and even that was not official at all, and not according to standard practice, especially in a public matter such as this, where it should be signed by members of the committee, or at the very least, they should confirm that so-and-so is sending the statement and that they vouch for it.

A general point regarding the above: If in every matter of Torah and mitzvos, one of the fundamentals is the quality of *zerizus* (alacrity)—and in the words of our Rebbe, the author of the Tanya, the *posek* in the hidden parts of Torah, and the Shulchan Aruch, the *posek* in the revealed parts of Torah: "It is known to all that the mitzvah of the virtue of *zerizus* in all mitzvos is stated and repeated in the words of our Sages... and the *zerizus* of Avraham Avinu, peace be upon him, is what stands for us and our children forever... a wondrous *zerizus* to show his joy and desire to fulfill the will of his Creator and to bring satisfaction to his Maker, and from him our Sages learned for the fulfillment of all mitzvos" (Iggeres HaKodesh, Ch. 21).

This is especially true regarding the restoration of the Shul named after the Tzemach Tzedek in the Old City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt, as the eyes of many are upon it, watching the progress of the matter, asking, inquiring, and learning a *binyan av* (a precedent), a *kal v'chomer* (an a fortiori argument), and a *gezeirah shavah* (a comparison) for many other matters.

In addition to what I wrote in my first letter, that in my opinion the aforementioned Shul is the heritage of all Anash in all corners of the globe, and every bit of progress there is progress that concerns all Anash in all corners of the globe—and from the "yes" you hear the "no," and a word to the wise is sufficient.

The summary of all the above is my proposal:

a) To hold an **urgent** meeting of all members of the management committee to investigate the reasons that caused the aforementioned alarming situation, and primarily to strive to find a way to immediately eliminate those reasons, and immediately adopt the entire aforementioned plan—in the language of Iggeres HaKodesh—with "wondrous *zerizus* to show their joy and desire to fulfill the will of their Creator and to bring satisfaction to their Maker," for it is certainly and surely the will of the Ribono shel Olam that the Tzemach Tzedek Shul and Beis Medrash in the Old City of Jerusalem be established.

b) To choose and appoint as soon as possible who the two signatories on the checks will be, and it would be best to have a third person as a substitute, meaning that every check must be signed by two out of these three.

c) It is understood that these two or three people must each be from the group of five who constitute the management committee.

d) To open a bank account in the name of this management committee, and it is certainly unnecessary to emphasize that it must be in a bank that has no concern of *ribis* (interest), i.e., that there is a clear and public *heter iska* there.

e) Based on past experience, I fear that there will again be a long delay until the above is put into practice. On the other hand, several Chabad funds in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt, are in need of financial resources. Therefore, from all the funds that remain after the expenses for the Shul repairs that have already been made, thousands of Lirot will remain in the Shul fund (with which they will open the bank account), and all the remaining funds should be transferred **immediately** to the Chabad institutions that receive support from here, according to the list from the secretariat on a separate sheet, and they have already been deducted from the account of these institutions.

f) From here on, the procedure will be that funds will be sent to the Shul fund after a detailed report of the past is received here, as well as a clear indication of what matter the additional sum is needed for, the size of the sum, etc., etc.

g) It has been emphasized many times in my letters, and yet for the sake of emphasis, I state it again: the sole and exclusive owner from here on of the Tzemach Tzedek Shul in the Old City is the Shul’s management committee.

h) For the sake of emphasis, I wish to stress one more point, although it is also understood and simple: that in everything written above, "the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek Shul in Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt," the intention is the Shul, its courtyard, the buildings in the courtyard, etc., etc., but everything follows the main thing, and therefore they were included under the name of the Shul.

Please confirm receipt of this letter by return mail, and it would be best if it were sent quickly and urgently, in the manner in which it is sent from here, for several understandable reasons. May it be the will of Hashem that within a short time you will be able to bring good news regarding the progress of the entire matter until its completion. And the merit of the Admur the Tzemach Tzedek will stand for each and every one to succeed in their efforts for the building of the Shul and its perfection with wondrous *zerizus* and with joy and a good heart.

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above,

M. Schneerson

P.S. A rumor has reached me that there is someone who wants to conduct a fundraising campaign, whether broad or not, for **anyone who wishes** to donate to the repair of the Shul, etc. As I have said orally on various occasions, all the expenses for the establishment and perfection of the Shul are the exclusive merit of those who study the Torah of the Tzemach Tzedek and follow in his ways to some extent at least, as well as public institutions and public funds, but not from private individuals who, for the time being, are not Anash, but only sympathizers or relatives—although after the establishment and perfection of the Shul, there will surely be a change in this, but that is a vision for the future.

## 9523

9523

B"H, 16 Tammuz, 5728

Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the class of
Rabbi Shabtai Alperin, may he live,
May Hashem protect them,

Shalom u’Bracha!

Your letter from Erev Shabbos Kodesh, Parshas Zos Chukas HaTorah, has been received.

May the Ribono shel Olam fulfill the heartfelt desires you write about for the good. May you be successful in the study of Torah and the performance of mitzvos with hiddur, permeated with yiras Hashem and ahavas Hashem. And may the statement of our Sages, of blessed memory, be fulfilled for each of you and for all of you together : **"You have labored"**—that you should exert yourselves and toil—and then comes the promise: **"and you have found"**—that you will find great success in all of this.

You are surely familiar with the story of 12-13 Tammuz, the geulah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, which reminds us of his mesiras nefesh for Yiddishkeit in general, and for chinuch al taharas hakodesh for Jewish children in particular, never being deterred by any obstacles.
