## 9724

19 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the distinguished, G-d-fearing, learned, and elevated individual, who seeks the welfare of his people and possesses noble character traits, a scion of a noble lineage, R' Schneur Zalman, shlita,

Peace and blessing!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the auspicious day of 13 Tammuz. As is the custom among our brethren, the children of Israel, to find hints and connect one matter to another, it is a good sign that your letter was received after today’s farbrengen.

Although on the face of it, it is puzzling to hold a farbrengen during the Three Weeks, the 12th–13th of Tammuz this year marked 75 years since the Bar Mitzvah of my father-in-law, the Rebbe. In connection with this, the maamarim that his father, the Rebbe [Rashab], said during the Bar Mitzvah celebration and throughout the following week—in the words of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, the "seven days of feasting"—were printed. These concluded on Sunday, 18 Tammuz, a postponed fast day; therefore, the farbrengen and the meal of the seventh day were held on Monday, 19 Tammuz, as explained in the *reshima* at the end of the booklet.

This is the reason for today’s farbrengen, albeit brief in duration, to review the content of the conclusion of the Bar Mitzvah maamarim, which is the matter of the day.

Upon returning from the aforementioned farbrengen, I found your letter dated 13 Tammuz, with two lines drawn under the **13 Tammuz**.

For this reason, I am hastening to reply to you and also to enclose the maamar *Tefillin D'Mari Alma* – 5653, which also contains excerpts from the *reshima* regarding the Bar Mitzvah.

Together with the above, I also received news today that the final volume of the Alter Rebbe’s Shulchan Aruch was brought to the bindery today. When they bring it back from the binder, two copies will be sent to you as you requested. May it be the will of Hashem that the Torah of the Alter Rebbe, the Baal HaTanya—the *posek* in the hidden dimensions of Torah—and the Shulchan Aruch—the *posek* in the revealed dimensions of Torah—illuminate our path and the path of every one of our people, the children of Israel, each one who is called by the name of Israel, to follow his path in life, as is the beginning (and foundation of the fulfillment of the entire) Shulchan Aruch: "Bold as a leopard, light as an eagle, swift as a deer, and strong as a lion to do the will of your Father in Heaven."

I read with special interest the lines regarding the Chassidic library in Kfar Chabad. The intention is surely that the content and the location should be in harmony—I mean that it should be a *Chassidic* library, not a library *about* Chassidus, fitting for the location of Kfar Chabad; that is to say, fitting for the founding intent of this village: a Chassidic way of life in daily living.

Forgive me for writing about this, for seemingly, what is there to say? But regarding people of a scientific bent, they require a special *iskafya* to forgo scientific debates (and refutations), to the extent of not bringing the views of those who fight and disparage the system at all, not even to bring them in order to refute them and disprove their conclusions.

And even though the point of "know what to answer" is well known, this is not the matter for a library open to all, for this is **not** the *avodah* of every individual. The intent of the Chassidic library is to open wide the gates of Chassidus to every single person, words of the Living G-d for the living people of Israel who are attached to Havayah, the Living G-d.

And although in the end, one should not fear the results of debate and conclusions, for we are speaking of the Torah of truth—and therefore, true science, debate *aliba d'emes* (for the sake of truth), and any debate worthy of the name (meaning a debate to seek the truth) cannot, Heaven forbid, disprove anything from our Torah, the Torah of truth—yet sometimes, and especially in our times, there stand young ruffians (in terms of character and the quality of truth) who advocate in the name of so-called scientific research and engage in debate and inquiry where the slogan is open and external—seeking the truth—but their intention is only to justify a preconceived notion. This notion determines the conclusion and the position of the proponent in advance, who consequently directs his research in a way that predetermines the conclusion. If the above is true regarding a platform or institution dedicated in principle to scientific debate, all the more so regarding a library and everything connected to it.

It is simple that when the time comes, all the Chassidic books published by Kehot will, G-d willing, be provided to Kfar Chabad, and the question about this is surprising.

Regarding your writing about our friend R' Ch. L. shlita, I have spoken with him several times about the matters you write about—and without any results; to put it more clearly—a refusal.

The affair of the Tzemach Tzedek shul in the Old City of Jerusalem is, understandably, most painful. Even a year ago and more, I began to urge the "matters" in writing and through travelers going from here to there. To my greatest regret, there is no progress at all commensurate with what should have been done in this regard.

Regarding your writing about the difference of opinion between so-and-so and so-and-so, etc.: in the beginning, when I proposed establishing a shul committee to manage all its affairs, I was especially careful not to propose individuals, but rather institutions. This is because of the inner nature of the matter, as I view the shul as the property of all the Chassidim of the Tzemach Tzedek, their students, and their students' students. Therefore, its ownership is in the hands of the institutions that are in the spirit of the Tzemach Tzedek and his students, and especially the institutions in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established.

[And what I called by name one of the committee members is because there is no possibility of holding a meeting of the entire Agudas Chabad and Tzeirei Agudas Chabad, etc., and I saw no other way but to call by name, and the wise will understand.]

Likewise, I did not want to call the people by name for the aforementioned committee, for one should not determine from a distance who will represent this institution or that institution; the institutions themselves must choose them and appoint them. And afterward, the committee must divide the roles.

These two reasons, and more, remain in full force even now.

By the way, that man whom you call by name, and who supposedly needs a visit here so that the relationship will be, etc.—I have heard much good about him in general, and especially regarding the spreading of the wellsprings at various gatherings and in certain circles, in a successful manner and with words that come from the heart.

These days I have written to the shul committee once again with urgency, and perhaps it will help.

Thank you for the good news regarding the construction of the houses in Kfar Chabad, and the hostel is surely included in this, although it is a bit surprising that you do not mention it explicitly.

Thank you also for the suggestion to speak with Mr. M. Yuviler shlita. What is on the agenda is for him to overlook his grievances. I mean that although the Chassidic encyclopedia has already been printed, except for about eight of the last pages, the matter is delayed because we are waiting for the proofreading of these pages, which must be done by me and requires me to concentrate solely on this. Therefore, it is postponed from time to time. It is worth influencing the aforementioned to forgo the fact that all the times set by his committee for the appearance of the first volume of the encyclopedia have already passed. It is surely known to the aforementioned that the entire encyclopedia has been printed, except for the aforementioned addition, since a printed copy, albeit unbound, was sent to his committee. And similarly regarding the series of books about the seven generations (starting from the Alter Rebbe until my father-in-law, the Rebbe), for which a time was also set for the appearance of the first volume, and it was delayed at the printer, even though it has already been typeset and proofread once, and now it is waiting to be arranged into pages. This is entirely dependent on the printer, for on our part the entire volume is finished, and I only need the printer's proofs. In this too, the aforementioned should forgo the fact that the deadline has passed, and therefore all the funds that were supposed to be given for the subsequent volumes of the encyclopedia and for the printing of all the series of books of the seven generations should be set, as if they were also fulfilling the time conditions. One must answer to this that the reason for the delay is not negligence, Heaven forbid, or the like, but rather an effort and hope that the matter will be more refined, improved, and perfected, etc.

As you concluded your letter, the matters are lengthy and all of them are practical, but I did not find in your letter an answer, nor even a reaction or hint, to what I mentioned there regarding the *Aluf* A. Sh. shlita in my previous letter. Perhaps the lack of reaction is also an answer, in accordance with what you write at the beginning of your letter—that there are matters you decided not to write about to me "so as not to complicate me." But since the matter also concerns the future, it would be good if there were clarification on this. And if you say that this is also a practical matter—practical in dimensions that—to use the flowery expression—embrace the world, and in my opinion, in the security, physical, and spiritual spheres. And the wise will understand.

In conclusion, similar to the opening, in the language I heard from my father-in-law, the Rebbe, that he said when he was born and also in the year of his Bar Mitzvah, that in both of them the fourth fast and the fifth fast, both the 17th of Tammuz and the 9th of Av, were postponed: May it be the will [of Hashem] that since they are postponed, they should be postponed—entirely—through the true Redemption, that they should be turned into joy and gladness. And the setting of this year as mentioned above, a setting that postpones the fourth fast and the fifth fast, should be turned into joy and gladness very soon.

With appreciation, respect, and blessing,

M. Schneerson

## 9525

B"H, 20 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To my dear relative, the G-d-fearing, Torah-learned, and distinguished man of character, who engages in communal needs, a man of many accomplishments and energy, etc. Mr. Yitzchak, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter of May 16th in due time, and I have been waiting to receive the two books you mentioned, expecting them to arrive at any moment. In fact, they only arrived in recent days (perhaps due to the strike that took place in France), and I hasten to acknowledge their receipt.

At the same time, I wish to express my hope that you, and indeed all Jews, will from now on be able to print and disseminate only good news, both in general and regarding individuals, and to do so in good health and high spirits—naturally, this also includes good news regarding your family.

This is especially pertinent as we have just passed the days of 12-13 Tammuz, the liberation of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory, a narrative with which you are surely familiar. You also know that for Jews— a stiff-necked people—a day of merit and a day of redemption that is connected to a specific event does not merely pass; it has a continuation, remains as such, and is regarded as a day of spiritual potency (yom segulah) year after year.

With blessings for good news in all respects,

My relative.

9526

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the Chossid, the man of action, involved in the holy work of building, [Rabbi] Chaim Yaakov Shlamme, Director of the "Beis Rivkah" Teachers' Seminary in Yerres.

Peace and Blessing!

In response to your letter from the day of the [Fast] of the Fourth Month—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—I have enclosed my [letter] to the graduates. If they require it, you may provide them with the appropriate explanation. [We have been promised] that words which come from the heart enter the heart and accomplish their effect.

According to the [words] of our Alter Rebbe, that "one does not argue with advice," I refrained from expressing my reaction to the following matter until I saw some hint that I should indeed voice an opinion on the subject. I found that hint in your aforementioned letter; once the hint arrived, the situation changed, and it became forbidden for me not to express my reaction. The matter is as follows:

I heard with the greatest astonishment some time ago from the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, Rabbi B.A. Gorodetsky [regarding] your thought of replacing your beautiful role in the education of Jewish girls—a role that is even more exalted, as it involves educating Jewish girls to become educators themselves when the time comes—[a matter of] "dipping in order to cause others to dip." For each of them is called, according to our Sages, a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, from which it is also understood that regarding each and every one of them, the adage holds true: [As is the mother, so is the daughter.] The magnitude of this matter is understood and is also simple, especially according to the [adage] of the Baal Shem Tov that the love of the Holy One, Blessed be He, for each and every one of the Jewish people is infinitely greater than the love of elderly parents for their only child born to them in their old age.

Yet, despite all this, you have entertained the thought of exchanging this sublime role and mission from the Holy One, Blessed be He, for a position of Rabbinate in our current times, etc., and a word to the wise is sufficient.

As mentioned, I did not intervene in this until now, as the matter was still in the realm of "being requested without having been asked," and furthermore, I was of the opinion that the matter would ultimately remain in the realm of mere thought—even though such a thought, as stated, evokes the greatest astonishment.

It is simple that everything written in my letter to the graduates applies many times over to the one who took the lead in guiding them until they reached the status of certified graduates with a diploma as a teacher in Israel, and even more so in terms of quality. Surely, for one such as yourself, further elaboration is superfluous.

I would only add one point: as I have heard several times from the aforementioned Rabbi B.A. Gorodetsky, your wife also has an active part in the establishment and development of the Teachers' Seminary, which means that she, too, would be exchanging her role and mission for something else.

It is understood that I have heard, also several times, from the aforementioned regarding the reasons that supposedly stirred this thought in you and your wife—that someone is interfering, etc. Even if one were to say that the situation is indeed so and there is no exaggeration, the solution to this is not to abandon the educational system and leave the role and mission, but rather to make an effort to nullify the interferences, or at the very least, to minimize them.

It is understood and simple that there is more to be said on this matter than what is written here, but surely for one such as yourself, even what is written will suffice. I will only add that I view the entire matter as a mere thought even now; yet, as mentioned, such a "thought" and "initial premise" are distressing and astonishing.

May it be the will of Hashem, the God of Truth, who gave us the Torah of Truth—the instruction for each and every person regarding their role in this world—that He guide you and your household in the path of truth and goodness in all details.

With blessings for good tidings.

## 9727

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the graduates of the "Beis Rivkah" Teachers' Seminary 
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

It was with pleasure that I received the good news that you have completed your course of study and have merited to receive your teaching certificates.

Surely, after your years of study at the "Beis Rivkah" Teachers' Seminary, founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, you understand the magnitude of the privilege, and alongside it, the magnitude of the responsibility that has been placed upon you to be teachers in Yisrael—

Or more accurately, not merely teachers who impart knowledge and wisdom to students and pupils, but rather—and this is the essential point—to teach them their path in life during their years of study and education, which will serve as the foundation for their path in life when they grow up and stand on their own. This is the true intent and central point of an education worthy of the name—preparation for a life worthy of the name; that is to say, a life according to the instruction of our Torah, the Torah of life.

It is explained in the words of our Sages that along with the role given to a person, they are first provided with the ability, the possibility, and the strengths to fulfill that role in its entirety and perfection.

And if this is true for any institution based on the purity of holiness, it is all the more so for an institution founded by my father-in-law, the Rebbe, Nasi of Yisrael, who throughout his life in this world sacrificed himself for the education of the sons and daughters of Yisrael in the purity of holiness—a literal mesiras nefesh—and who even now arouses great mercy for the success of all those who resolve to fulfill the general role of a man and woman in Yisrael in this world, which is to serve their Creator, and the role of those chosen ones who have merited to be educators in Yisrael, educating the younger generation.

May it be Hashem’s will that you carry out all the above with the appropriate dedication and commitment, and with joy and a glad heart. May Hashem grant you success in this, and may the blessing of Hashem accompany you in all your affairs.

With blessings for success in all the above and for good tidings,

M. Schneerson

9228

9228

B"H, 22 Tammuz, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi and Chossid, man of action and accomplishment, etc., [Rabbi A.G.](#_ftn_772) may he live.

Greetings and blessings!

Enclosed is [a copy of two letters](#_ftn_773).

Regarding what I wrote in my letter to Rabbi S. regarding my view of the entire matter as a *kassad* (preliminary thought/initial premise), the meaning is simple: If the aforementioned individual truly desires it, he should continue his position at Beis Rivkah just as he has until now, and even with greater intensity, even if there were some promises made to him regarding a rabbinical position, etc. This can also be explained according to Halacha. However, the main point is the desire of the aforementioned individual and his wife—whether one of them or both together.

The aforementioned individual does not know that a copy of the letters was sent to you, and I rely on your insight as to whether or not to disclose this to him.

With blessings for good news.

P.S.

Enclosed is a letter from the esteemed Chossid, etc., [Rabbi Ch.M.A.](#_ftn_774) may he live. Since our Sages of blessed memory [instructed us](#_ftn_775) to "honor him and suspect him," in this case as well, I am concerned that despite his telling me clearly that the visit is only to clarify the situation, he will speak about the necessity [of moving from there](#_ftn_776) to the [neighborhood of](#_ftn_777) our friends the Rabbis Zevin, Wolf, and the like, while adding frightening rumors that, G-d forbid, there might be an undesirable change for our Jewish brethren, and so on.

Since in my opinion—and I told him (Rabbi Z.S.) this—it is clear that this is a rumor they fabricated in order to frighten and pressure people to move, etc., as they have already done several times and in several places (and a word to the wise is sufficient), I fear he is under pressure to speak in the spirit of those who sent him, etc.

Therefore, it is necessary that after the aforementioned individual leaves—which is expected to be for a duration of nine days—you should find a pretext to visit Rabbis [Matosov](#_ftn_778), Pinson, and perhaps also Lipsker and Djerba (since it is in his plan to visit all these places). You should find an opportunity to strengthen the hearts of our Jewish brethren so that they will not be afraid at all; not only the institutions—even those not affiliated with Chabad—should continue their activities, but also private individuals. And in an appropriate manner, raise the greatest concern regarding the spiritual alienation of the youth who are moving to the Zevin-Wolf neighborhood under terrible pressure, the details of which are surely known to you. As long as there is no actual change to prevent the aforementioned alienation and coercion, it is understood that one cannot rely at all on any kind of promises, etc., etc.

It is also understood that since they promised Chabad that the youth who were educated in Chabad institutions will from now on [be directed](#_ftn_779) to Chabad if they so desire, and also because of the relations in the Zevin neighborhood with Rabbi Z.S.’s associates here, there is no point at all in *tzuraysn zich mit zei* (clashing with them) if it is not absolutely necessary. Therefore, it is good that there be a certain interval between your visit to the aforementioned places and Rabbi Z.S.’s visit, so that the underlying intent will not be so emphasized. For this reason, as mentioned above, you must also find a pretext for your trip to Matosov, etc., for a different purpose (and a word to the wise is sufficient).

All of the above is written based on conjecture and a likely concern. You will certainly know more details from Rabbis Matosov, etc., regarding the visit and the discussions, etc., and consequently, the situation will be clearer to you, and you will know what is necessary to negate, etc., etc.

May it be the will of Hashem that the mission in your hands succeeds in calming the spirit of our Jewish brethren wherever they may be, to establish their standing and situation in both material and spiritual matters, and to establish and develop our institutions in every respect, with joy and good tidings.

Your letters from the 3rd and 7th of Shevat were received, as well as the check for ten (which I may have already acknowledged) and for eight.

## 9531

[9531](#_ftn_807)

B”H, 15 Menachem Av, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the Board of Directors of the Tzemach Tzedek Shul in the Old City of Jerusalem, may it be rebuilt speedily by Moshiach Tzidkeinu,
May Hashem grant them life,

Shalom u’Bracha,

Following up on my previous letter, which I am certain was received in due time—though it is surprising that it has not yet been acknowledged—since the time it was sent, I have received your letter dated 22 Sivan and the one following it. In them, you write regarding the decision concerning the signing of checks, the treasurership, and the bookkeeping, although even in those letters there is no information regarding any actual progress.

2) There was an approach made here, with considerable force, by Mr. G. shlita, who visited the Shul during his stay in Eretz Yisrael t”v over the last few weeks. As is his custom everywhere, he prefers to make such visits without prior notice; therefore, he did not meet anyone from the Shul’s management, the congregants, etc. However, he saw and “witnessed with his own eyes that nothing has been added to the repair of the building since his last visit there several months ago.” During his subsequent visit with our friend shlita, he expressed his profound astonishment regarding this, as well as his protest against the aforementioned conduct. He was left with the impression that our friend identified with him in this matter, and the Mayor also joined him, and he too agrees—and even more so—that the sum he donated should be returned, etc.

It is surely unnecessary to add that, as is the nature of any donor, and especially regarding a significant sum, **it is impossible to enter into arguments and negotiations with him, especially when he says that he himself saw and checked, etc.—which, incidentally, is his way with institutions to whose benefit he contributes.**

It is not my intention to cause you distress, but since this concerns practical matters, I have come to point out that although regarding the sum he donated—since one does not divert funds from one charity to another, and since the Shul is not being built or repaired, the sum he donated specifically for this purpose will be returned to him in any case—this affects Mr. G.’s attitude toward other institutions here and in Eretz Yisrael t”v, as well as regarding the dental clinic, in addition to the influence on our friend, etc., etc.

I have delayed sending this for **several weeks** in the hope that, perhaps, there would finally be some **actual progress**—but it seems I have not yet merited hearing good news in this regard.

With respect and with blessings for good news,

On behalf of the Rebbe shlita,
Nissan Mindel – Secretary

## 9,737

[9,737](#_ftn_817)

B”H, 15 Menachem Av,
Erev Shabbos Nachamu, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

[Mrs.](#_ftn_818) Yocheved Wolf-Reich, may she live,

Blessings and peace!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from the Ninth of Av—may it soon be transformed into joy and gladness—in which you write regarding the need to establish an institution for children with special needs, where they will be educated according to Torah and mitzvos, etc., continuing from your previous letter on this matter some time ago.

I believe I already shared my opinion on this with you at that time, but in any case, I will reiterate it here: The reality in Eretz Yisrael, may it be rebuilt and established, is that for such an undertaking to be realized in a practical, beneficial, and good manner, it must be attached to an organization that already has an existing infrastructure. This is especially true regarding fundraising, and in many cases—particularly in a project of this nature—it will require the involvement of the Ministry of Welfare, the Ministry of Education, etc., and that the appropriate political figures take an interest in it as well.

Enclosed is a clipping from a newspaper discussing the establishment of an institution similar to the one mentioned, as well as who is participating and working on it, etc., which also reinforces my aforementioned assessment.

Certainly, since you are on the scene, you can clarify further details regarding this. It is possible that the approach used by the initiators of the institution mentioned in the aforementioned newspaper could also serve to realize the project about which you are writing.

As for the great value and importance of the matter, it is understood that no one needs an explanation; however, due to our many sins, this alone is not enough to bring the matter to fruition, and the wise will understand.

With blessings for success in your activities in education on the purity of holiness, and for good tidings in this.

[mazkir1]On behalf of the Rebbe, may he live,[/mazkir1]

Secretary

## 9,338

[9,338](#_ftn_819)

[19 Menachem Av, 5728]

**Question**

Regarding the sicha on Rashi, s.v. *Livanecha* (to your children), these are the students:

a) On the verse *Beni Bechori* (My firstborn son), Rashi explains it as an expression of greatness, and states there that this is the *peshuto* (simple meaning) (and not the explanation of *bechor*—firstborn)[A].

b) Shabbos 89b: "When they said 'we will do' before 'we will hear,' you called them 'My firstborn son.'" Rashi explains there that it was revealed before You that they were destined to say before You at Sinai "we will do and we will hear," to accept Your yoke with love, like children.

c) In Tanya, Chapter 2, it is implied that both verses refer to the *neshamah*[B].

* * *

**Response:**

a) 1) After all, even according to this—it was before Matan Torah.

2) It has been discussed many times that **all** that is brought in Rashi on the Torah—must be (according to Rashi’s **own** statement)—the *peshuto* of the verse (and if it is impossible—Rashi says "I do not know" (for even there, there is an explanation of our Sages, and this is well-understood))—except that within the *peshat* itself, there can be levels, etc. Consequently, the continuation of Rashi **in that place**—(Shemos 4:22)—**and his Midrashic explanation** a) is also according to *peshat* (only not as simply). b) Furthermore (and this is the main point): it proves that the explanation that they preceded [the angels] **is not** sufficient, etc. And this is well-understood.

b) It is not according to the *peshat*.

c) And with the emphasis that this is the level of the *neshamah* from its **own** perspective (and not from the perspective of the receiving of the Torah—and not like the Sifri and Rashi here, that "you are children, etc."—this is from the perspective of Matan Torah. Although, with some difficulty, it could be explained [otherwise]).

## 9,339 

B”H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To all participants of the N’shei U’Bnos Chabad convention
In the Holy Land, may it be rebuilt speedily, in Kfar Chabad
May Hashem grant them life,

Blessings and peace!

I was pleased to receive the news regarding the fifth national convention, which will be held, G-d willing, on the first day of Parshas Shoftim — *Shoftim v’shotrim titein lecha* — which is Rosh Chodesh Elul, the [month] of mercy and favor. I note the theme of the convention: **The Crown of Attributes** — **Tzniyus**.

May it be the will of Hashem that your efforts succeed in inspiring good deeds in this direction, illuminated by the light and vitality of Chassidus, regarding the strengthening of Tzniyus and its dissemination in your immediate and extended surroundings. For Tzniyus is the crown of glory of the daughters of Yisrael, each of whom is called a daughter of Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah — the daughters of Yisrael everywhere, and all the more so in the Holy Land, the [land] upon which the eyes of Hashem your G-d are from the beginning of the year until the end of the year.

It is well known [what our Sages of blessed memory explained] that Tzniyus is the essence of holiness.

A special role in this belongs to the Jewish woman, who is called the [Akeres HaBayis] — the foundation of the Jewish home, both for the individual and for the collective. Corresponding to this responsibility and role is the magnitude of their reward, as explained [in the holy Zohar]: to draw down blessings into the home and family — *birkhan d’leila u’birkhan d’lata, b’usra, b’banin, u’v’bnei banin* (blessings from above and blessings from below, wealth, children, and children’s children).

And as a hint in the beginning of this week’s Parsha — [when each one] fulfills within the collective of Yisrael, "Judges and officers shall you appoint for yourself," then judgment below nullifies judgment above, and one merits to be inscribed and sealed for a good and sweet year.

With blessings for success in your avodah and for good tidings in all the aforementioned,

M. Schneerson

## 9540

9540

B"H, Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, and may Hashem fulfill your heart’s desires for the good in all the matters you write about.

[Especially](#_ftn_828) as we are entering the month of Elul, the [month](#_ftn_829) of mercy, the concept of which is explained in the well-known parable of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch (Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32):

It is like a king who, before entering his city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc.

This is the concept of the month of Elul, for then He is in the state of "a King in the field," a time for the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy.

May it be the will that each of us utilizes these auspicious days to draw closer to our Father, our King, by increasing our involvement in Torah and mitzvos with hiddur, and may Hashem receive the prayers and requests of each [and every one](#_ftn_830) of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, with a pleasant and smiling countenance, for good and for blessing.

With blessings for a *kesivah v'chasimah tovah* and for good tidings.

## 9,543

Furthermore, beyond the essential point—fulfilling the command of Hashem to "increase in holiness" —every addition in matters of goodness and holiness increases Hashem’s blessing in everything that you and your families require. And surely there is no need to remind you of the greatness of your merit, and along with it, the greatness of your responsibility, as each one of you is a daughter of our matriarchs Sarah, Rivkah, Rachel, and Leah, who built the House of Israel.

As we stand in the auspicious month, the [month](#_ftn_837) of mercy and favor, these days are especially propitious for making resolutions and taking positive actions in the direction mentioned above.

M. Schneerson

## 9,544 

B"H, 5 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the students of the Chabad Yeshiva summer camp in Lod,
May Hashem keep them alive.

Peace and blessing!

I received your letter and your request for a *pidyon nefesh* with pleasure, along with the photographs. May the *Ribono shel Olam* fulfill your heart’s desires for the good, that you may succeed in all the work of your hands, both materially and spiritually, and become *Chassidim*, G-d-fearing, and scholars.

It is unnecessary to emphasize that this depends solely upon you, for there is nothing that can stand before the will ; on the contrary, one who comes to purify himself is assisted.

These days are days of *segulah*, days of the month of mercy and favor, the essence of which is explained in the well-known parable of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the *Tanya* and *Shulchan Aruch* (*Likutei Torah*, *Parshas Re'eh*, 32) :

It is like a king who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc.

This is the concept of the month of Elul, when He is in the state of "King in the field," a time of the revelation of the Thirteen Attributes of Mercy.

May it be the will that each one of us, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*, utilizes these days of *segulah* to draw closer to our Father in Heaven in truth and with inwardness, by increasing our involvement in *Torah* and *mitzvos* with *hiddur*. And may the *Ribono shel Olam* receive the prayers and requests of each and every one of us, within the entirety of *Klal Yisrael*, with a pleasant and smiling countenance, for good and for blessing.

With blessings for success, for good tidings, and for a *kesivah v’chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 9745

[9745](#_ftn_844)

B”H, 5 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, one who engages in communal needs, etc.,
[Moreinu HaRav](#_ftn_845) Shlomo Yosef, may he live,

Shalom u’Bracha!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter from Rosh Chodesh Elul and the enclosure.

I hasten to reply, so as not to delay a matter that should not be [delayed], etc. You write that you saw (in the additions to the Shulchan Aruch) that **I** cited a source for the statement of our Rebbe in the Siddur [regarding the fact that](#_ftn_847) one passes every single day in the performance of the great Tanya. And likewise in [Shaar](#_ftn_848) HaKollel — however, the aforementioned is **not** from me, but was copied from what is written **(as noted there).**

What is recorded in my notes regarding this from a **long** time ago (and I do not recall the chain of events regarding this now, and the seforim are not currently at hand): It was brought and discussed at length in Responsa Imrei Yosher, Vol. 2, by Rabbi Meir Arik. And it is not like the Rashash in Menachos 66a. And the Levush writes similarly in Orach Chaim 551. And the Responsa Maharam Schick, Orach Chaim 287, raises a difficulty on this from Kiddushin 29b. See also Avnei Nezer, Orach Chaim, Vol. 2, 559; Yoreh Deah, Vol. 2, 395; Divrei Malkiel, Orach Chaim, Siman 17; Pri HaSadeh, Vol. 2, 16; Minchas Pissim, Orach Chaim 249.

With blessings for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah*, for health, and for good tidings,

M. Schneerson

I have received reports that there is talk [suggesting](#_ftn_849) that our friend, shlita, is setting out on a tour of various countries of the children of Cham and the like. And although, on the face of it, this is "not my business," etc. — in my opinion, it is not a matter at all, and he should fulfill and have fulfilled in him [that which is written](#_ftn_850): "Happy are those who dwell in Your house" (meaning, all of his holy work). And regarding such matters — it is much easier and more pleasant to nullify them when they are still in the stage of mere talk, etc. And if this opinion is accepted — surely you will find a way and a manner to act in the aforementioned direction, and to succeed, with the help of Hashem.

## 9546

[9546](#_ftn_851)

B”H, 9 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and blessings!

In response to your letter of 27 Menachem Av and those preceding it,

It is surprising that your involvement in the shidduch for your daughter, tichyeh, does not seem to be with the necessary vigor. May it be His will that, at the very least, from here on in you proceed with added vigor and added strength, and may it be fulfilled that [you have labored](#_ftn_852) and found, and may it be soon.

Regarding the proposals you write about, it makes little difference which one you begin with, as it appears from your letter that the information regarding each of them is good. To avoid having to ask about this again, you should begin with whichever one is more practical to pursue immediately. It is not of great consequence which yeshiva he learns in, provided that he is a yirei shamayim, etc.

To expedite this matter even further, this letter is being sent as express and urgent.

I trust that you have received from the esteemed chossid, etc., etc., [our teacher](#_ftn_853) R' Ephraim, sheyichyeh, the sum on account of what is due to you for your holy work in the affairs of the Reshet as compensation for your time, and the monthly sum as we discussed during his visit here. You will surely provide an accounting of how much more is owed to you.

From all of the above, it is understood that the suggestion to visit here together with your son, sheyichyeh, etc., does not seem appropriate to me. On the contrary, you should increase your holy activities in the Reshet Ohalei Yosef Yitzchok, where they will mention you at the tziyon; and you should increase your vigor regarding the shidduch for your daughter, tichyeh, as well as regarding what I have spoken to you about many times concerning your own personal situation—I refer to the matter of a shidduch, and a word to the wise is sufficient.

Surely there is enough time and energy to attend to all of the above simultaneously, especially since your holy work in Eretz HaKodesh assists you in this. I look forward to good news.

With blessings for success and for a *Kesivah V’Chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 9747

[9747](#_ftn_854)

B”H, 10 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, G-d-fearing, etc., engaged in communal needs, etc.
[Rashi](#_ftn_855) [shlita],

Greetings and blessings!

I was pleased to receive your letter, in which you inform me that the hearts of the descendants of the esteemed Rabbi, the esteemed Chossid, and G-d-fearing, etc., R’ Boruch Mordechai, of blessed memory, of Babruysk—one of the greatest students of the Alter Rebbe—have been stirred to commemorate him—

During the week of the parsha, "When you come [tavo](#_ftn_857) to the land which Hashem your G-d gives you as an inheritance... and you shall go to the place which Hashem your G-d will choose,"

[And when they came](#_ftn_858) to Jerusalem, it was an inheritance, an eternal inheritance; and Rabbi Shimon bar Yochai said: both this and that—rest and inheritance—[refer to Jerusalem](#_ftn_859).

And the commencement is on the Shabbos Kodesh preceding it, [from which](#_ftn_860) all the days are blessed, which is also the yahrtzeit of the aforementioned Rabbi and Chossid, of blessed memory—

To commemorate his memory by establishing a collection of seforim in Nigleh and Chassidus at Yeshivas Toras Emes—founded by our Rebbes, the Nesi’im—in Jerusalem, the Holy City, may it be rebuilt and established speedily in our days.

May it be the will [of Hashem] that this collection of seforim succeeds in its goal and purpose, in the words of the one whose yahrtzeit is being observed, [in his approbation to the sefer Likutei Torah](#_ftn_861) of the Alter Rebbe: "These seforim of the house of the Rav will illuminate the branches of holiness; the one who sees them will say, 'It is morning' [i.e., the dawn of redemption], etc.," to ignite the hearts (of all those who study and engage in them) and to draw the hearts of Yisroel to their Father in Heaven.

And in the style of the continuation of that same approbation: Let us show gratitude to his (the one whose yahrtzeit is being observed) descendants, who will surely expand this library as much as is needed, both in quantity and quality. The merit of the many depends upon them—all those who study these seforim and engage in their words to increase Torah, the Torah of Emes, and to glorify it, until we merit [the fulfillment](#_ftn_862) of the prophecy:

That knowledge, wisdom, and truth will increase, [as it is said](#_ftn_863), "For the earth shall be full of the knowledge of Hashem," with the coming of that King [who will arise](#_ftn_864) from the seed of Dovid [and will teach](#_ftn_865) all the people and instruct them in the way of Hashem, etc.

With blessings for success in the founding and expansion of the aforementioned library, and with blessings for a *kesiva v’chasima tova* for all those participating in the founding celebration and the Shabbos preceding it, and in the establishing and expanding of this endeavor, shlita, and for good tidings in all of this,

M. Schneerson

## 9548

[9548](#_ftn_866)

B"H, 11 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the esteemed, G-d-fearing, and distinguished individual, who engages in communal needs, etc.,
R' Moshe Tzvi, may he live [HaLevi](#_ftn_867)

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated Erev Rosh Chodesh Elul . . .

[Regarding the content](#_ftn_868) of your letter:

1) Regarding the scope of your future activities to "serve the public" — based on the [adage](#_ftn_869) of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, "The past teaches the future": [You have already succeeded](#_ftn_870) (and to a great extent) in bringing the matters and light of Yiddishkeit (and Chassidus in particular) to many circles, including those to whom (at least for the time being) only you have found the approach — and you should continue in this in the future as well (especially during these days of hisorerus of Elul and Tishrei, and similar holidays and festivals). And, of course, with the emphasis (in summarizing your activities) [that the deed](#_ftn_871) is the essential thing.

2) And it is obvious (though to my great surprise it seems your thinking is otherwise — and therefore I am writing this explicitly) — that you certainly must not forgo your good custom and your greatest privilege: blowing the shofar at the Kosel HaMa'aravi on Motzaei Yom Kippur. Fortunate is your portion that you have merited this, etc.

949

By the grace of Hashem, 12 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To Mr. Ariel Aluf [Sharon],

Shalom u’Bracha,

I acknowledge with thanks the receipt of your letter from 24 Av, which arrived with some delay, and I apologize for the delay in my response.

Regarding the content of your letter, as we discussed here—I am in complete agreement with you regarding the liberated territories, etc., as we discussed at length. However, to my regret, I do not agree with you that a shift in public opinion in our Holy Land will influence a change in the stance of the circles that make the decisions on this matter. According to my information—from sources that have been reliable until now—there is no change whatsoever regarding the **actual** position of the aforementioned circles. I only wish that the shift in public opinion would succeed in changing, at the very least, the unofficial stance that is being implemented in practice: preserving the Arab character of the Old City of Jerusalem (based on the argument that one must maintain the status quo as it was envisioned for this part of the city at the time of its capture last year, for it is against "justice and fairness," etc., to exploit the conquest to impose something upon the residents who were found there at the time of the conquest). The consequences of this stance are understood, both in practice and in day-to-day life, especially since they believe they fulfill their obligation to the Jewish public by settling our brothers, the Children of Israel, in the **surroundings** of the aforementioned part of the city.

It is understood that I am writing this to you unofficially and personally, for it is not my way to speak disparagingly of the Children of Israel, especially those who have the power to accomplish great and wondrous things in the matters mentioned above, yet do not do so for various strange reasons—and, on the contrary, act otherwise.

It is also understood that the intention of this letter is not to blame anyone—for what use is there in such blame?—but rather to express my sorrow, at least in writing, to you and to those to whom, in your opinion, it would be beneficial to convey the contents of these lines.

If this is the situation regarding Jerusalem, the Holy City, then all the more so—how much worse is the situation regarding Chevron, where only Arabs reside and it was never a place for the Temple, etc. The Arab settlement there is established and developed, and according to reports, even grand—all of which reinforces the stance mentioned above even further. Despite this, they investigated and inquired about the possibilities of establishing a yeshiva, etc. I received a clear answer that "it would be better for me" to interest myself in a yeshiva in Jerusalem rather than in Chevron. It is understood that among the settlers (despite the stance of the aforementioned circles), there are several Chabadniks (some openly and some in secret), and you are certainly aware of the status of the settlers and their situation there, which is not far from the situation of prisoners, etc. The explanation is also as above, based on "justice and fairness." The common denominator for all these phenomena is: what will the "great" world say, etc.? And as we discussed during your visit here.

For example, if—Heaven forbid—there were to be a conflict between an Israeli youth and an Arab youth in Chevron, and since the Arab youths outnumber the Children of Israel there, it is possible that, Heaven forbid, the Israeli youth would suffer blows, **etc.** On whose side, in your opinion, would the Israeli military police stationed there stand? Especially if the mayor (who, it seems, had a part in the riots and the pogrom in Chevron, may Hashem protect us) were to raise a clamor and shout about the provocations of the Children of Israel, etc.

This is also the reason why I "asked" you when you were here about the background and the reason for the manner of the conquest of the Old City of Jerusalem last year, where so many of the elite of the Israeli army fell in battle, **disproportionately** to the casualties on other fronts.

Incidentally—and perhaps it is not merely incidental—you still owe me an answer to this (as we discussed when you were here, that you would investigate and answer me). The information I received on this—and as mentioned, from a source that has been reliable until now—and as I said to you in our conversation, was that there was an instruction and command (without room for appeal) from above. I only wish that I am proven wrong, even though my speaking with you on this was in the style of a question and allowing room for doubt.

Furthermore, my question on this was not out of curiosity, Heaven forbid, regarding such a painful matter, but rather to point out the train of thought of those who gave the aforementioned instruction—many of whom are still in positions of power today. To our sorrow, and perhaps also to our shame, no shift has occurred in their outlook, for even then it was known in advance that this would cause more casualties. From this, it is also understood regarding the situation in Chevron and Jerusalem, etc., now.

It is also understood that I do not despair, Heaven forbid, of a change in the aforementioned situation. But until then, there is no place or **practical** benefit for anyone to issue a call to ascend and settle in Chevron—even those who would not actually respond, and it would only be a matter of propaganda and expressing a train of thought. And all the more so for those who have good prospects that their call would lead to actual ascension, and consequently, to a clash with the aforementioned stance and to sharp differences of opinion **and decrees** against those who ascend—which would be revealed to the public, and not only to the Jewish public but also to the nations, who would see that those who make the decisions are restricting the settlers and those who ascend, and even more than restricting, etc., which is a disgrace and an encouragement to the spirit of the enemies of Israel.

Despite all this, as mentioned, I do not despair. Rather, it is not a shift in the opinion of the Jewish public that will effect change, but the mistakes of the Arabs and those who support them. As it was in the past, such mistakes forced the "peacemakers" last year to finally agree to defense, and consequently, to a war of momentum. I only wish that in the future this will be in an easier manner and will not, Heaven forbid, touch the life, body, or even the property of our brothers, the Children of Israel, anywhere they may be.

It is wondrous to what extent the title given to the Children of Israel in our Torah, the Torah of life, "a stiff-necked people," not only stands in its full force to this very day, but is being exploited in a way that is the opposite of the Torah and the vital interests of the people of the Children of Israel. An example from the very last few weeks: the hijacking of the El Al plane by the Algerians. Everyone saw clearly the reaction even of those who seemingly should have been among the friends of the people of Israel, and despite all this, they proclaim "thank you" to the nations of the world for the solution that was found, the "victory of morality in this," etc. And even if you were to say that it was necessary to agree to the extortion (in order to save lives), etc., who forces one to crown so-and-so as a moral person, a perfect tzaddik, and a model for the masses, etc.? But one should not question a stiff-necked people, as mentioned.

And the matter of being stiff-necked in the belief in the kindness of the nations (despite the announcement of our prophets and seers that "the kindness of the nations is a sin") is so great that even the Czech invasion did not weaken or shift this superstitious belief. And although, seemingly, the matter of Czechoslovakia is not related to the content of this letter, there is an internal connection: it shows the state of mind of some of those who determine the course of events in our Holy Land—a course that is expressed in actual deeds, deeds that are painful, sorrowful, and also worrying regarding the future (at least the near future—until they depart from their aforementioned stance).

We conclude with a good thing: giving thanks for the warm regards that you conveyed during your visit to Kfar Chabad, which, according to the letters and reports I received from there, were words coming from the heart and with warmth. It added encouragement and strength to them, which everyone needs, and they in particular, especially in these days full of events, and in a land "which Hashem your G-d seeks out from the beginning of the year to the end of the year," as is written in our Torah. On the other hand, there are enemies surrounding it, and from day to day one sees more points of weakness in the attitude toward them on the part of the government in our Holy Land, which in their opinion must behave toward them with silk gloves and extreme caution. If there is a conflict between an Arab and an Israeli, the first thing that must be clarified is what they will say in the capital of this or that country, and decide what to do accordingly. Therefore, from time to time, the enemies allow themselves more acts of rioting, and all the more so, provocations, and from riots to sabotage, etc.

As we approach a new year, according to the well-known formula, may it be the will that this year and its undesirable phenomena come to an end, completely and absolutely. And for the coming year, and even in the final days of this year, may the blessings begin, including a fundamental shift in the aforementioned stance, without waiting for undesirable events that will necessitate the change. After all, you have seen miracles from Hashem, the Almighty, in the recent past, and He is all-powerful to perform miracles such as these and more, and in the traditional phrasing—in a revealed and manifest good.

Enclosed are four newspaper clippings as examples.

With respect and blessing for a *Kesivah Vachasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year to you and all your household, may they live,

M. Schneerson

As mentioned above, because of the painful points in this letter, it is written to you personally, but you have permission to show it or convey its content to whoever, in your view, it would be beneficial.

I will conclude with the hope that—befitting my letter to you, which is written with an open heart and at length—you will respond to all the points in it, also in the aforementioned manner, in addition to the answer to my aforementioned question and other questions that you hoped to clarify and answer after your return to the land.

## 953

[953](#_ftn_906)

B"H, 18 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the congregants, and the Gabboim at their head, of the Ahavas Yisrael – Chabad Shul in Bnei Brak, in our Holy Land—may it be rebuilt and established by Moshiach Tzidkeinu speedily in our days—

May Hashem preserve them and may they live.

[On the birthday of the two great luminaries](#_ftn_907), the Baal Shem Tov, after whom your shul is named, and the Alter Rebbe, founder of the Chabad approach,

I wish to express my hopes and wishes that your shul and beis medrash will surely go from strength to strength in the avodah of tefillah—as a shul—and in public shiurei Torah (both nigleh and Chassidus)—as a beis medrash—and in the recitation of Tehillim at opportune times, especially on days of segulah. For the book of [Tehillim](#_ftn_908) is the bridge between Torah and tefillah, the section of praises and hymns within the twenty-four books of the Tanach.

And the Faithful One hears the prayer of His people Israel with mercy, especially in [gates](#_ftn_909) distinguished by Halacha, to accept their prayers and fulfill their heart’s desires for good [from His](#_ftn_910) full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

Especially in light of the information I received from the esteemed Chossid, a man of fine character, R' Chaim Nachman Kovalsky, may he live, who is involved in the organization and leadership of the shul and beis medrash, you will surely continue to proceed with this strength with even greater intensity and vigor, [ascending](#_ftn_911) in holiness from one level to the next.

[And these](#_ftn_912) are days of segulah, days of the [month](#_ftn_913) of mercy and favor, the nature of which is explained in the well-known parable of our Rebbe, the Alter Rebbe, author of the Tanya and Shulchan Aruch (Likutei Torah, Parshas Re'eh, p. 32):

"It is like a king who, before entering the city, is met by the townspeople who go out to greet him in the field. At that time, anyone who wishes to go out to greet him is permitted to do so, and he receives them all with a pleasant countenance and shows a smiling face to everyone, etc."

May it be the will of Hashem that each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, will utilize these days of segulah to draw closer to our Father in Heaven, in truth and with inwardness, by increasing in matters of Torah and mitzvos with hidur. And may Hashem, blessed be He, receive with a pleasant and smiling countenance the prayers and requests of each and every one of us, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, for good and for blessing.

With respect and with the blessing of *Kesivah v'chasimah tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 9550

[9550](#_ftn_921)

B”H, 24 Elul, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Greetings and Blessings!

I acknowledge receipt of your letter and the enclosure.

May Hashem Yisbarach fulfill your inner wishes for the good in all the matters about which you write.

It is certainly superfluous to emphasize that daily conduct in accordance with Torah—Toras Chaim—and mitzvos, [v’chai](#_ftn_922) bahem, in addition to the primary point that this is the will and commandment of the Ribono shel Olam, is also the path to receiving His blessings in everything one needs.

In response to your question regarding your family situation, there is a clear instruction in our holy Torah—Toras Chaim, hora’ah b’chaim (a guide for life)—that one must act with the proper energy—naturally, in a manner of tzniyus—regarding a suitable shidduch for you. And since the Torah states this in a categorical form, it is certain that this is good for all who may be involved; in this case, good for you and good for your daughter, shetichyeh.

It is also self-evident that it is not so easy to find a suitable shidduch, but for this there is the [promise](#_ftn_923) **yagata umatzas**—that if one acts energetically and with good kavanah, the Ribono shel Olam helps and one is successful. And it is surely unnecessary to emphasize to you that an increase in kvius itim l’Torah and the performance of mitzvos b’hiddur adds to the blessings of Hashem Yisbarach.

In connection with these current days of segulah of the [month](#_ftn_924) of Elul, yemei harachamim v’haratzon, you have surely heard the [explanation](#_ftn_925) of the Alter Rebbe, Baal HaTanya v’HaShulchan Aruch, regarding the nature of these days, through the parable of a king in the field before he enters the city, when anyone can go out to greet the king, and the king receives everyone with satisfaction and a smiling countenance.

May it be the will that Avinu Malkeinu fulfill the requests and tefillos of each one of us, within the entire Klal Yisrael, for good and for blessing.

With the blessing of ksivah v’chasimah tovah for a good and sweet year, in both gashmius and ruchnius.

## 9796

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

Mr. Avraham Tobias, Netanya

Peace and Blessing!

I have just received the two issues of the publication, from the months of Sivan 5766 and 5768, along with your letter. I am sure you will also send the remaining issues as you mentioned in your letter, and I thank you in advance.

Since every matter occurs through Hashgacha Pratis, I will take the liberty of drawing your attention to the responsible and highly significant role you hold as the editor of these publications, which are read by many of the youth of Bnei Yisrael. Regarding each and every one of them, our Sages have said that a single soul of Yisrael is an entire world. Even when the material is written by others, much depends on the editing—what is omitted, what is added, and the like—and primarily on encouraging those suitable for it to write in the appropriate field and in the desired manner. And even if someone comes and says that it is not within the editor’s authority to change too much, if the matters touch upon the true values of our people, the Bnei Yisrael—that is to say, those founded upon the appreciation of our Torah, Toras Emes, and its instructions—then it is certainly the editor’s duty to publish words of truth and to reject matters that are the opposite of truth. This is especially true when dealing with publications for the youth, meaning those who are in the period of education and the shaping of their character and the nature of their soul for the years to come, throughout their entire lives.

It is understood that the argument is well-known that in a democratic regime, everyone has the right to stand by their opinion, etc., but this does not justify assisting in the publication of matters that are the opposite of Toras Emes and its mitzvos, which were given by Elokim Emes.

And based on the above—that everything is through the Hashgacha Pratis of the Creator of the world and its Guide—certainly, along with a task, and especially an important and serious task, one is also given the strengths and the possibilities to fulfill the task in its entirety. Furthermore, this can be done in ways of pleasantness, which are the ways of Torah, as it is said: "Its ways are ways of pleasantness."

With respect and blessing for good tidings in all the above, and with the blessing of *Kesivah V'chasimah Tovah* for a good and sweet year.

## 958

B"H, Days of Selichos, 5728
Brooklyn, N.Y.

To the sons and daughters of Israel, wherever they may be,
May Hashem keep them and grant them life,

Greetings and blessings!

One of the primary themes of Rosh Hashanah is—as has been emphasized many times—that it is the time of the **hachtarah** (coronation) of the Ribono shel Olam, the King of Israel and King of the world. This is bound up with our deep tefillah and inward petition: *Meloch al ha’olam kulo*—"Reign over the entire world!"

Such a petition implies a complete readiness to place oneself in a state that is in harmony with this Divine coronation. This means: to entirely submit and surrender oneself to the King, to the point where the very existence of the person and everything he possesses belongs only to the King. This is the concept of **kabbalas ol malchuso yisbarach**—"accepting upon oneself the yoke of Divine sovereignty"—which finds expression in all the details of daily life.

* * *

In truth, every day there is the concept of kabbalas ol malchus shamayim, especially when we recite Krias Shema. However, there is a fundamental difference: every day, the concept of kabbalas ol is the beginning and the underlying foundation for one’s conduct throughout the day, so that all of one’s affairs should be built upon kabbalas ol. But Rosh Hashanah is the time when kabbalas ol malchuso is **the** theme and content of the day; it is **revealed** and permeates the **entire existence** of the person, such that he becomes entirely batul to Elokus.

In order for this kabbalas ol to be complete and genuine, a person must first make a *cheshbon tzedek* (a true accounting) of his conduct until now, with a deep feeling of regret and teshuvah for the things that were not as they should have been. A true teshuvah washes away the negative and makes him *ahuv v’nechmad karov v’yadid* (beloved to the Ribono shel Olam, and an esteemed krov and friend). He becomes worthy, and it is certain that the Ribono shel Olam will accept his hachtarah and fulfill his petition of *Meloch al ha’olam kulo*.

* * *

Every era and every place has its own special advantages and special difficulties.

In our era, there prevails in various circles a drive for self-reliance and independence—not only in material respects but also in ideological ones: a drive to not want to submit to established order, to not acknowledge things before one understands them completely with one’s own intellect, and so on. Seemingly, this is an obstacle to the concept of kabbalas ol.

Particularly in countries that are still (relatively) young and were built upon the foundation of, and through, individual initiative and energy—and where this spirit characterizes the entire approach to personal and social life—this makes it even more difficult to fit oneself into the framework of kabbalas ol.

Notwithstanding all this, we have the principle that the Ribono shel Olam does not demand of a person things that are beyond his strength. Since kabbalas ol malchuso yisbarach is the inner content of Rosh Hashanah (and the foundation for all deeds of the entire year), and this is valid for **all** times and places, it is certainly possible—and indeed mandatory—that even in our times and in the aforementioned countries, one must arrive at a complete kabbalas ol malchuso.

In truth, there is also a special *ma'alah* in this—precisely in our time and in the aforementioned countries: A person who is not oriented exclusively toward independence, but is sometimes one way and sometimes the opposite, does not have the concept of kabbalas ol deeply ingrained in him; for him, it is no novelty to feel regret and change his position. Conversely, one who is not accustomed to submitting and is independent in his train of thought—when he arrives at the conviction that he must acknowledge a higher authority, it permeates him more deeply and thoroughly, and he finds the strength to transform himself **entirely** and **permanently**.

And this finds expression in him not only in feeling and intellect, but also in his machshava, dibbur, and maaseh (thought, speech, and action), down to the smallest detail. On the contrary, since the greatest part of the day is filled with deeds and speech, his kabbalas ol malchuso finds expression primarily in his speaking and doing, in the fulfillment of the mitzvos maasiyos, and in all the details of his daily conduct.

At the same time, this brings him to a more serious and energetic fulfillment of the mitzvah of **v'ahavta l'rei'acha kamocha**, especially regarding kabbalas ol malchuso yisbarach: to influence another Yid, and more Yidden, that they too should accept ol malchuso, and that for them, too, it should not remain merely in intellect and feeling, but should also find expression in machshava, dibbur, and maaseh in daily life.

* * *

May it be the will that this kabbalas ol malchuso yisbarach should immediately bring about the *kabel b'rachamim uv'ratzon es tefilaseinu* (accepting our tefillos with mercy and willingness), and may our Avinu Malkeinu grant each and every one, within the entirety of Klal Yisrael, a *shanah tovah u'mesukah* in all respects, in goodness that is visible and revealed—from His full, open, holy, and expansive hand.

With the blessing of *kesivah v'chasimah tovah*,

Menachem Schneerson

## 989

[Elul, 5728]

Mr. Eliyahu Amikam, may he live.

Peace and blessing!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter dated the 6th of Elul, the content of which is a survey regarding the subject of the renewal of the Sanhedrin.

As is known, I am accustomed to refraining from participating in matters such as these, for various reasons. However, noting that you connect the survey with "the widening rift between the majority of the Israeli population and the religious institutions, etc., on one hand, and on the other hand, the danger of assimilation threatening the majority of the Jewish people in the lands of the Diaspora," as you write at the beginning of your letter; and knowing that you are a serious writer for whom serious problems hold significance, and that you are accustomed to expressing your opinion fearlessly; and that your approach to the aforementioned problem undoubtedly stems from a heart torn and seething over the situation in general—I have decided to depart from my custom and respond to your questions.

Now, the survey itself regarding the renewal of the Sanhedrin—which revolves around three questions: (a) whether I see a need for the renewal of the Sanhedrin, (b) if so, how I envision its form, and (c) if not, the reasons for my opposition—is based, as mentioned, on the assumption that the situation in Eretz Yisrael (may it be built and established) and in the Diaspora raises the issue of religious authority, and that the renewal of the Sanhedrin is, as it were, the remedy for the situation. And I ask you: from where do you derive this? Is it true and correct that the renewal of the Sanhedrin is a remedy, and furthermore, the *only* remedy, for the situation prevailing in the spiritual and religious life of our people today?

If there were truly a dispute and a lack of order in many matters in the realm of Halacha, where certain doubts had arisen in the clarification of Halacha, and the great Torah scholars were divided over them—some saying one way and others saying another—and according to Halacha itself it were impossible for the matter to be clarified for practical application except solely through a Sanhedrin, which has the power not only to issue a final ruling but also to enforce its observance, or that all those who were divided in their opinion would be sworn and committed to submit to the Sanhedrin’s decision without hesitation or doubt—if the situation were such, the magnitude of the yearning of those circles who desire the renewal of the Sanhedrin, in order to nullify the dispute and bring peace to the world, would be understandable.

But let us examine if this is the reality. The proof of this: let us look at the situation regarding all those matters of Torah and mitzvos that are completely clear and not subject to dispute; are they observed by all the aforementioned circles? And in general, do all those participating in this survey, or in the question of the renewal of the Sanhedrin in general, submit to the authority of the Torah, believing that it is Torah from Heaven—both the Written Torah and the Oral Torah—and that it is a *Toras Chayim* (a Torah of life), from the word *hora'ah* (instruction), instruction and guidance in all the life of the individual and the life of the public and the entire nation, in every detail of daily life? For if that were the case, it is known to every student that even in the absence of a Sanhedrin, Israel is not widowed, and the Halacha determines how to act even in places where there are doubts regarding matters that, according to Halacha, only the Sanhedrin can clarify. Therefore, precisely in those circles that are G-d-fearing and who observe the mitzvos of the Torah in practice and with precision, despite the magnitude of their yearning to merit seeing the renewal of the Sanhedrin at the time designated for this in our holy Torah and in the appropriate manner—precisely in these G-d-fearing circles, no confusion is seen due to the absence of the Sanhedrin, nor is there felt among them a clamor for the renewal of the Sanhedrin, nor is the lack of religious authority felt so much in their private and public lives to the extent that there would be room, Heaven forbid, for those concerns mentioned in your letter.

And as for those demanding the renewal of the Sanhedrin who are not devoted and committed to the Torah and its mitzvos, it is clear that they do not recognize the essence of the Sanhedrin and do not know the nature of this matter, or that they have no intention from the outset to obey the Sanhedrin. For it is clear that the Sanhedrin has no power to waive even a *kutz shel yud* (the serif of a letter) from the Torah, and its entire purpose is only to instruct according to the Torah, and to stand guard so that its judgments are brought from potential into action, without fear of any person or any thing, and without submitting to anyone except the will of the Ribono shel Olam as revealed in our holy Torah. Consequently, those who think that through the renewal of the Sanhedrin various "stringencies" will be removed and various prohibitions will be permitted in the life of the individual and the public are mistaken. Aside from the error itself in the yearning for leniencies, which stems from the stubbornness of the heart and the casting off of the yoke of morality, etc., there is no room at all for these "hoped-for" changes.

Likewise, those who think that through the renewal of the Sanhedrin the rift between those who observe the Torah and its mitzvos and those who for the time being oppose the Torah and its mitzvos will be mended are mistaken. For it is clear that even with the renewal of the Sanhedrin, the number of the thirty-nine prohibited labors on Shabbos will not decrease, nor will anything be eased in matters of family purity and modesty, nor will there be compromises in kosher education based on the purity of holiness, and so on and so forth.

The conclusion from what has been said is that the cause of the aforementioned rift is not the absence of the Sanhedrin, and therefore the remedy is not in its renewal. Rather, the only rectification is that all those who have influence in all the circles of this generation recognize the truth, admit it without shame even if they erred in their previous outlook, and publicize their opinion and conclusion within all circles: that the foundation of the existence of the nation is solely the observance of the Torah and mitzvos in daily life, without compromises and changes, for "the house of Israel is not like all the nations."

And as for the actual renewal of the Sanhedrin, and the phrasing of the survey according to the three aforementioned questions, one must answer them all at once: anyone who examines the laws of appointing a Sanhedrin and knows who is qualified according to Halacha to appoint a Sanhedrin, and who is qualified to be a member of the Sanhedrin, etc., it will be clear to him that just as it was impossible for the Sanhedrin to be renewed from the day it ceased until now, so too have the obstacles and impediments to its renewal according to Halacha not ceased even now. And any organization that is called by the name "Sanhedrin" without regard for the Halacha, it is understood that this is nothing but a great deception and in no way will it be considered a Sanhedrin; its entire purpose will be only to mislead, and it will cause more damage than it will rectify, and it will not bring even the imagined gains.

But the true preparation for the renewal of the Sanhedrin is, as mentioned, through the fact that everyone who has the power to influence the restoration of the crown of Torah to its former glory, and to strengthen and disseminate the observance of the Torah and mitzvos in daily life, should do so with courage, and not be ashamed before the mockers. And it is in the power of each and every one to do so, each according to his status and situation, to remove the causes for which the Sanhedrin ceased, and to bring closer the true redemption through Moshiach Tzidkeinu, at which time the prophecy will be fulfilled: "And I will restore your judges as at first, and your counselors as at the beginning," etc.

With respect and blessing.

Certainly, from this point forward, you will fulfill this ruling. May it be the will of Hashem that you succeed in this.

## 9793

[9793]

[5728]

There is no place, specifically in this year—and even following the victory of the Six-Day War—to change one’s conduct on Yom HaAtzmaut. Nor is there a basis for the perspective of celebration; for after such open miracles, the expression of joy should have been through an increase **in matters pertaining to the One who performs the miracles**—namely, Torah and holiness. Instead, we see that, on the contrary, there has been a growth in the sentiment of "my strength and the power of my hand" (**and they do not even emphasize the mesiras nefesh** of those who fought). Even though the high-ranking officers themselves admitted that "it was the hand of Hashem," and everyone felt this—especially the heads of the army, who knew the forces on each side and the natural odds that contradicted the reality of the war’s outcome **and the manner in which it occurred**—the expression of joy proves the exact opposite... Especially since even those who were accustomed to reciting Hallel should not have recited a blessing over it, nor the blessing of Kiddush and others, for these are blessings in vain. **It can be said** that this applies even to the blessing of Shehecheyanu—**and many of the rabbis of Eretz Yisrael** ruled that it is forbidden to recite a blessing over the Hallel, **and they ruled that it should not be recited at all.**

The situation and the lawlessness are distressing, where even small ones—who have no ruling in this matter—slander the rabbis of Yisrael who forbade reciting a blessing over the Hallel on those days and forbade reciting it entirely, disparaging their honor, with no one to open their mouth and protest, etc.

**Addition**

## 974

[974](#_ftn_974)

B"H, 20 Marcheshvan, 5728
Brooklyn.

To the esteemed and G-d-fearing, etc.,
R' Avraham Elazar, may he live, Halevi

Greetings and blessings!

I hereby acknowledge receipt of your letter, which included a request for a blessing and a *pidyon nefesh* dated the 12th of Marcheshvan.

At an opportune time, it will be read at the *tziyun* of my father-in-law, the Rebbe, of blessed memory.

With blessings for proper *parnassah* and for good tidings,

M. Schneerson

I trust you are keeping up with the three *shiurim* that are appropriate for everyone—*Chumash*, *Tehillim*, and *Tanya*—and in any event, you should do so from now on.

Regarding your writing about the proposed partnership—seemingly, it requires clarification: 1) If everything is in order, why are they conceding and offering you 40% in exchange for your investment and labor? 2) What are you expected to "add" to the work beyond what you are currently doing? 3) The clause regarding restrictions (that they will continue... without you; that they will purchase from the business with a 5% markup on the principal, even though the profit margin, even in wholesale, is generally much higher; and more)—this requires further study. 4) How will the proposers divide their energy, etc., between their separate business and the joint one, especially since all of this is in the same location (at least in part)? 5) The settlement of old debts? 6) The valuation of the business. **And more.** You should certainly consult about all this with friends of yours who are merchants in similar fields, and decide accordingly.

Seemingly, the proposers should have ensured all of this themselves—rather than having it raised from across the sea.
